Kong sent Secretary Zhang Zhongqing to meet with them instead, saying that it was difficult to change the laws, and did not grant their request, and advised the representatives to still comply with the original measures. If there are any detentions or other incidents due to misunderstandings, the Ministry of Finance will give them fair treatment. (Special dispatch, 9th)

Jiangning Opium Smoker Registration Deadline 57

(Nanjing) The Jiangning Anti-Opium Association originally set the end of last month as the deadline for opium smoker registration. Considering the circumstances, the deadline was extended by ten days from October 1st. Now that the extension has expired, registration has been extremely enthusiastic. Over 7,000 people have registered in each district. After the registration closes on the evening of the 10th, the number of opium smokers and the amount of opium consumed will be tallied and reported to the Provincial Inspectorate for the allocation of opium soil. Registered opium smokers will be issued licenses. Those who continue to smoke privately without registering will be strictly arrested by the investigation division under the supervision of the Public Security Bureau and dealt with according to military law. Regarding opium soil sales, the entire county will be divided into four districts, with one opium paste shop in each district, and each shop will oversee a certain number of opium retail stores. Currently, over twenty households have requested to operate opium paste shops from the association. Their assets and guarantees will be carefully examined, and those who qualify will be selected by drawing lots on a scheduled date. (9th Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The Currency Reform and Unification Committee, prepared by the Ministry of Finance, is ready. Yuanxin Village has been selected as the location for the committee, and it will be established in late October. (9th Dispatch)

Ma Yinchu Discusses the Silver Problem 59

(Nanjing) Ma Yinchu said that the only way to stop the export of silver is for the Chinese people to unanimously boycott foreign goods. At the same time, the government should strictly enforce the absolute use of domestic goods for clothing, food, and housing. In this way, the amount of exports can be offset, and silver will naturally not flow out. (9th Dispatch)

Exemption of Licorice Paste from Taxes 61

(Nanjing) The Ningxia Construction Department submitted a request to the Ministry stating that Yuning Licorice Paste should be exempt from taxes. The Ministry investigated and found that Ningxia is located in a remote western region with a backward economy, and licorice is a major product. To promote industries in the border provinces, all Zhangdu customs duties on licorice paste manufactured by the company will be exempted. Provinces through which it passes must not levy any taxes in order to facilitate sales and encourage production. An order was issued yesterday to Zhangdu Customs Supervisor and the provincial finance departments to comply. (9th Dispatch)

Completion of Tata Golden Bridge in Ganzi County 76

Xining, Yushu News: Ganzi County in northern Xikang is an important route between Kangzang and Qinghai. The Yalong River, 73 miles away, runs through the county from north to south. The river is wide and the current is rapid. It can be crossed by leather boat, with three or four people per crossing. Livestock swim across, and many are drowned during the summer and autumn floods, causing suffering to travelers. After the Dada Golden War, the garrison planned to build a wooden bridge across the river, named Tata Golden, to commemorate the victory over Dada Golden. It is a thousand feet long and forty feet wide. The project was huge, and it is now completed, providing convenience for travelers. (9th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Henan Province Reorganizes County Militia 77

(Kaifeng) The Provincial Security Department is reorganizing the county militia in all counties. It is stipulated that the provincial security teams will be divided into four regiments, with the amount of self-defense surtax in each district as the standard for whether the militia is retained or eliminated. If the militia expenses exceed the surtax, they will be appropriately reduced or reorganized. After the reorganization of the provincial security teams, all expenses will be统筹统支 by the Provincial Security Department to control and prevent abuses. (9th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Situation of Rural Cooperation in Jiangxi Province 78

(Nanchang) Jiangxi divides rural cooperation into five districts. The Lianxin Fuxing District has established 1,590 societies with 104,772 members. The Economic Commission has allocated a foundation of 500,000 yuan, of which more than 350,000 yuan has been loaned to various societies. (9th Dispatch)

Chiang Cables Ten Provinces to Strictly Enforce Opium Prohibition 79

(Nanchang) The Headquarters announced that Chiang cabled on the 5th to Henan, Hubei, Anhui, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Fujian, Jiangxi, Hunan, Shaanxi, Gansu, and other provinces to follow the opium prohibition law. Planting will be prohibited in the 23rd year, and no opium seedlings will be allowed to emerge from the soil next year.

If opium planting is found, or military and police officials are found to be shielding it, they will be dealt with according to military law. (9th Dispatch)

Replacement of Police Officer at Japanese Consulate in Xiamen 80

British Cargo Ship Sailors Rescued 81

(Hong Kong) The sailors of the British cargo ship "Cambridge City" were completely rescued this afternoon. The rescuers risked their lives in a storm to drive the rescue boat of the Suffolk cruiser ten miles, and because the water on the beach was shallow, they towed the rescue boat for another two miles before rescuing the sailors. The Suffolk cruiser personnel's fearless and courageous rescue was highly praised by the shipping company. The rescued crew members are now on their way to Hong Kong aboard the Suffolk. The "Cambridge City" and its cargo are believed to be completely lost. (9th Reuters Dispatch)

International Commercial Telegram 83

丨Reuters Exclusive Commercial Report, October 9丨

Gold and Silver: London Gold Price: The London gold price today is 142 shillings and 9 pence, up 3 pence from yesterday.

London Silver Bar: The London silver price rose by 0.375. The spot price is 20 pence and 25, and the futures price is 23 pence and 375. Speculators bought, so the price rose. Later, Chinese bankers sold, and speculators also sold at high prices, but the silver market closed steadily.

Mumbai Silver Bar: The Mumbai silver market was tight and stable today, rising 3 to 4 annas. The closing price for spot was 63 rupees and 4 annas, November futures were 63 rupees and 5 annas, and December futures were 63 rupees and 8 annas.

Exchange Rate: British-American: This morning, the pound continued to decline in the London foreign exchange market. The official market occasionally used the equalization fund to adjust it. There were not many transactions. The opening exchange rate between the British pound and the US dollar was 4 dollars 90 cents 375, lower than the closing exchange rate between the British pound and the US dollar yesterday.

At noon, it fell again by 4375 to 4 dollars 89 cents 9375. At 2 pm, it fell again by 375 to 4 dollars 89 cents 5625.

British-French: The opening price was 73 francs 96, the same as the closing price yesterday.

At noon, it fell by 6 pounds to 72 francs 90. At 1 pm,

It fell again by 6 pounds, but there was no change at 2 pm.

US-British: The pound fell in the New York foreign exchange market. The opening exchange rate between the US dollar and the British pound was 4 dollars 89 cents 25, which was 1.625 cents lower than yesterday. About 20 minutes later, it fell another 25. This is the latest price.

Cotton and Wheat: American Cotton: The cotton market opened with a drop of 15 pounds due to a large amount of sales. Before long, it fell another 2 pounds, but the mood turned better and buying emerged, mostly from the same industry. The price recovered by about 7 pounds. There were not many transactions when the telegram was sent.

The price has not changed.

Indian Cotton: Prices fell in the Mumbai cotton market due to long liquidation and speculative selling. The closing price for White Loh Ki cotton for April-May was 206 rupees, down 2 rupees 75.

British Cotton: The Liverpool cotton market plummeted today. At 1 pm, the price for January futures was 6.52, down 12 pounds from yesterday's closing price.

British Wheat: The Liverpool wheat market rose today. At 1 pm, the price for December futures was 5 shillings 3 pence 125, up 375 from yesterday's closing price.

American Wheat: The wheat market opened quietly. Speculators did not make any trades. The opening price fell by 0.25 to 0.50. Later, due to good news from Liverpool, the market stabilized slightly. The latest prices were unchanged from the opening prices, and some rose by 0.25.

Rubber: London: The London rubber market was quiet. At noon, the transaction price for January-March futures was 7 pence, down 0.125.

New York: The rubber opening price plummeted, 21 pounds lower than yesterday's closing price. The market remained unstable, and selling was strong. The price at 10:40 was 16 pounds lower than the opening price.

Chairman Chiang in Hankou

General Headquarters Expansion Anniversary Week Admonishment 85

Promote Politics with Emphasis on Rural Construction

Hankou Dispatch: Chairman Chiang, at 7:00 AM on the 8th, summoned Wang Shuchang, Commander of the Pingjin Garrison, and Guo Chiping, Chief of Staff of the Western Route Army Headquarters of the Five Provinces, to the Xingyuan (temporary headquarters). After inquiring about their situation, he crossed the river at 8:30 AM to attend the General Headquarters Expansion Anniversary Week. Senior personnel from the Party, government, military, police, and academia first gathered at the headquarters. At 9:00 AM, Chiang arrived in full military uniform amidst solemn silence, leading the attendees in formal salutations. He then delivered an admonishment, the original text of which has been organized and published as follows:

"Deputy Commander Zhang, esteemed officers, today I have come to Wuhan and happened to coincide with the Premier's Memorial Week. I would like to take this opportunity to share my observations with everyone. I haven't been to Wuhan for a long time. This time, upon inspection, I have seen great progress in all aspects, whether political, military, police, or municipal. It is evident that all military and civilian officials have been working together diligently to fulfill their duties. Judging from the current state of Wuhan, the future of the country is certainly filled with great hope, and we will definitely be able to achieve our goal of saving the nation. This is something that brings me great comfort. However, no undertaking, especially in politics, can hope for great success overnight. To achieve great things, one must be able to uphold the spirit of 'unceasing self-improvement,' and continue to work hard. On one hand, we must strive for progress day by day, and on the other hand, we must accumulate gains day by day. Only in this way can politics be fundamentally transformed. Then, the foundation of everything in politics can be built day by day according to the goals of our ideology. Although the political foundation in Wuhan has not yet been firmly established, it can be said that a preliminary framework has already been formed. Now that we have such a framework, as long as everyone can make progress in spirit day by day, I believe that in the future, all reform and construction efforts in politics, military affairs, society, and education will be able to advance simultaneously. We will certainly be able to lay a solid foundation to fulfill our mission of saving the nation. Regarding the political measures in Hubei, when I was about to leave Wuhan in the 21st year of the Republic (1932), I promulgated the 'Eighteen Articles for the Reorganization of Hubei Politics.' Now, two years have passed. Based on this outline, I have examined and found that although many things have been done and there has been great progress and achievement, there are still many things that have not been done, or even started. In fact, the things in the outline are the most urgent and simplest preliminary measures. Now that two years have passed and they have not been fully implemented, I, as the person who promulgated the outline, feel very ashamed. Therefore, today I will recite these eighteen articles again, hoping that everyone can work together to fully realize them in the future. 1. Implement the system of administrative supervisory commissioners, ensuring that they can fully exercise their powers. Prudence in the selection of county magistrates and public security bureau chiefs, their performance should be thoroughly evaluated, guaranteed, and strict reward and punishment regulations should be enforced.

2. The existing police and local self-defense security teams in each county should be strictly reorganized, their organization improved, their numbers verified, their source of funding secured, and their public or private firearms guaranteed. They should be thoroughly trained, with special emphasis on political knowledge and martial arts. 4. After the security teams and other local self-defense teams in each county have been reorganized, the term of service for conscripts in each county, including regular, reserve, and auxiliary forces, should be stipulated, and jurisdictions should be divided to integrate internal affairs into military orders. The Security Department should prepare an implementation plan and proceed in phases. The first phase of the reorganization work should be completed by March of the 22nd year of the Republic (1933). 5. Implement the household registration system based on the Regulations for Compiling and Investigating Baojia Household Registration, and ensure that the compilation and investigation are completed within the prescribed time limit according to the compilation and investigation schedule. In case of special circumstances that make it impossible to complete the process within the prescribed time limit, a factual report may be submitted for approval to extend the deadline, but the extension should not exceed March of the 22nd year of the Republic. The entire province must complete the process uniformly, and a review should be conducted from May to September of the same year. 6.

Except for the budgets of the Hubei Provincial Government and the Hankou Municipal Government, which have been reviewed and approved, the revenue and expenditure of all local expenses of the county governments and their affiliated agencies throughout the province should be compiled into formal budgets, submitted to the Department of Finance for review and approval, and promulgated for implementation. Starting from February of next year, all expenses should be implemented in accordance with the new budget. 7. The establishment of the Provincial Farmers Bank and credit cooperatives in each county should be preliminarily completed by March of the 23rd year of the Republic (1934). 8. The land survey should be completed within five years, but the preliminary plan for the first year of the 22nd year of the Republic should be stipulated as soon as possible. 9. All financial institutions should immediately implement the accounting system. 10. All levels of financial personnel must obtain guarantees, and the competent authorities should conduct thorough supervision at all times. If there is any case of embezzlement or fraud, they should be strictly pursued for compensation and punished according to the law. 11. The Provincial Department of Construction should temporarily prepare a one-year road construction plan and proceed in phases. The first phase of work should be completed by March of the 22nd year of the Republic. 12. Hubei's dike and water conservancy projects should be transferred to the National Economic Commission for unified planning, and the Jianghan Engineering Bureau, affiliated with the commission, should be responsible for management, in order to save expenses and prevent overflow. 13. In the counties of Hubei, especially in the bandit-affected areas, in addition to striving for rural revitalization in accordance with the Land Management Regulations and the Rural Cooperative Regulations, appropriate areas should be selected to establish collective farms to test the latest farming and management methods. 14. Primary and secondary school education should stimulate students' national consciousness in various courses and cultivate the spirit of sacrifice for the country. 15. Primary and junior high schools should conduct military training for boy scouts. 16. Schools above junior high school should emphasize military education and militarize students' lives. 17. The literacy movement for civilians should be planned for one year by the Department of Education, starting from Hankou. 18. All levels of judicial organs should complete the clearing of lawsuits within a time limit. In the future, civil and criminal lawsuits should be concluded within one month in accordance with legal procedures, so as not to burden the people with litigation." The eighteen articles were the outline for the reorganization of Hubei politics that were established at that time. Among them, there are several very important things, such as compiling and investigating baojia household registration, measuring land, compiling formal local budgets for each county, promoting cooperative enterprises in each county, and establishing collective farms. Some of these have not been done well, or have not yet started. It is hoped that they can be actively implemented in the future and completed as soon as possible. It is not just the civil affairs officials who should work hard to do this. All senior military officers in the areas where they are stationed should also implement all political measures within their respective areas, cooperate with local civil affairs officials, and earnestly follow the outline. Do not think that these matters belong exclusively to the scope of civil affairs and that military officers can ignore them. Only in this way can politics and military affairs advance together, bandit suppression can be thoroughly successful, and all localities can have a truly clear and bright day. This is the meaning of hoping that all military and civilian officials will work together in the future to earnestly implement the matters stipulated in the outline for the reorganization of Hubei politics. Secondly, as a result of the observations in recent days, although Wuhan has made great progress in all aspects, there are still several points that need special attention in any aspect, whether political, military, municipal, or military affairs. First, whatever we do, we must pay attention to reality, be consistent inside and out, and not just talk about a superficial form. For example, in terms of the cleanliness of roads, the roads are generally cleaner everywhere now, but if you look at the secluded places on both sides of the roads, there are still inevitably dirty places. Scraps of paper and garbage are scattered everywhere. Also, like the situation in ordinary agencies throughout China, things look generally neat on the surface, but if you go inside and take a look at the kitchen and the toilets, many of them are unbearably dirty. These places, which are most prone to the spread of germs and infectious diseases, are not paid attention to by people who only care about form and not substance. This accumulated habit is really a common problem of the Chinese people. For example, an ordinary family often only sweeps the middle of the house, and the corners of the walls and doors are never swept. The life of a Chinese family is like this, and the same is true for everything in society and politics. Therefore, I want to specifically raise this point today and talk to everyone, asking everyone to correct it if they have it, and to encourage themselves if they don't. In the future, no matter what you do, you must pay attention to reality. You, as the leading officers, must pay extra attention to the places where malpractices are most likely to occur, which others are most negligent of, and which are actually the most important to rectify. This is a fundamental key to our work.

The same is true in politics, military affairs, and society. For example, when leading troops, you should not only know how to drill every day, take classes, or conduct routine inspections of internal affairs. You must pay close attention to the management and hygiene of all aspects, especially the toilets and kitchens. You should be diligent in inspecting these places. As for the things that the Public Security Bureau manages, they are especially complicated, and everything must be based on facts. For example, in terms of cleanliness, have all the public security bureaus and posts in Wuhan thoroughly met the requirements of cleanliness? I hope that you, as the leading officers, will pay extra attention to this. This is about striving for reality in doing things. Second, all our measures should not only pay attention to cities in the future, but also pay more attention to rural areas and remote alleys. For example, the roads in Wuhan are very clean now, and the New Life Movement has been implemented step by step. As long as everyone can continue to work hard in the future, there is no need to worry about not doing well. However, our work is not just about improving cities. You should know that the affairs of cities are only one or two percent of our entire work.

The remaining 98 or 99 percent are in the counties and rural areas. What is the situation in the county seats and rural areas of Hubei now? According to what I have seen during my inspection, the state of disorder and uncleanliness is not only similar to what it was before the 21st year of the Republic, but also no different from what it was thirty or forty years ago. It can be said that there has been no progress at all. Not to mention the situation in other places, even in Wuhan, everything in the city, whether it is roads, parks, police administration, finance, or education, has progressed, and the form is very impressive. However, as long as you go a little further, such as to the areas of Hankou and Liujiamiao, there are especially many poor people and dilapidated thatched huts. Although a road has been opened, the nearby streets have not been improved. Drains and other facilities related to public health and social education that are beneficial to the general poor people have not been paid attention to at all. Little do they know that if you do not pay attention to these places, various problems are likely to occur. In this way, even if the city is doing very well, there will be no complete success. Moreover, any knowledgeable person, whether Chinese or foreign, will never only pay attention to the facilities in the city when they look at our politics. They will definitely pay extra attention to how you are doing in rural areas and whether you are paying attention to the welfare of the general poor people. Yesterday, I met two foreigners who were inspecting there. At a glance, they knew that the Chinese government only focuses on the roads in the city and does not pay attention to the rural areas outside the city, and cannot seek benefits for the general poor people. Also, the New Life Movement that we are doing now is not only about improving the lives of the general people in the city. The purpose is to make the lives of all citizens in the country, from large cities to remote villages, regardless of men, women, old, young, rich, or poor, universally improved, so that they can meet the conditions of "neatness," "cleanliness," "simplicity," "frugality," "promptness," and "certainty," and conform to the spirit of propriety, righteousness. Therefore, everyone must pay special attention to the countryside and the most poor and dirty places in the future, and think of various ways to improve them first, and create more benefits for the most poor people. This is the second point that I hope everyone will pay special attention to in the future. Third, we must do things from top to bottom and use the spirit of diligence to make up for the lack of material things. Nowadays, people generally want money first for everything. They say that they cannot do anything without money. This statement is generally considered reasonable, but it is actually wrong. Many ordinary things do not necessarily require money to do. For example, to make a place clean, it does not necessarily require building a sewer. It is also possible to simply dig open ditches to drain flowing water. This thing does not necessarily require money to do. We can just draw a line through the police and assign the local baojia chiefs or street chiefs to be responsible for each household to dig it.

Wouldn't that be a success? Even if the people do not have working tools, we can provide them with tools from the police station and lend them to them. That doesn't cost much money either. For example, the last two weeks, I walked through a place in Hukou and other counties, and there were many usable stone strips lying around randomly. The county government did not pay any attention to organizing them. When I asked him, he said that he had no money and could not start. In fact, these things do not need any money. As long as the county magistrate pays a little attention and asks the village and town baojia chiefs to guide the general people to spend a little effort and organize them, many national objects can be used, and many unclean places can be cleaned up. Things like this are all the chronic diseases of the Chinese people from top to bottom. We must thoroughly change them in the future. We must understand that the ability of our revolutionaries is to be able to lead the general people by setting an example and using the spirit of diligence and hard work to make up for our lack of material things. Even if we do not have money, we can do things well. We must also understand that land is money, and the labor of the people is even more of a resource for production. As long as we can think of ways to make full use of the land to increase production and use the people's labor to transform society, we can do many things without money. Guanzi's saying "to teach the people to be strong by death, and to teach the people to be rich by labor" means that we want to make the country and the general people strong, we must make them understand the great righteousness of life and death, break through the barrier of life and death, and be able to cultivate their spirit of courage to sacrifice for the country. The latter sentence is to make the people accustomed to labor. Therefore, the meaning of "the people's livelihood lies in diligence" is that the government should be good at using the people's labor to increase the welfare of the people themselves. Nowadays, people generally think that to do a career, they must first have money, and then they must think of ways to raise money, levy taxes, and exploit the people. Little do they know that if a person cannot do anything without money, this person will definitely not be able to do anything even with money. Moreover, to exploit money from the people is to exploit them to the point of completion and to destroy the country. Only by making good use of the people's labor to increase the interests of the people themselves is the right way to revolutionary construction. Only by making good use of labor is it beneficial and inexpensive, and inexhaustible. Only by using it to increase the welfare of the people themselves will it be hard work without complaint and inexhaustible use. Therefore, the Nanchang Xingying had a circular order stipulating that every strong man should do three days of work for the country every year.

If this method can be universally implemented, each county, excluding the old, young, and women, will have an average of 50,000 strong men. Each county will have 150,000 obligatory laborers every year. As long as the government can use them with a reasonable plan, whether it is for repairing dikes, dredging rivers, or building roads, isn't it

Continued on page thirteen

Page 13

There is a large project that can be completed. This method of conscripting labor,

In the beginning, for two or three years, the government may have to force it. After a few years, the people will get real benefits and become accustomed to it. Naturally, they will trust the government and be able to automatically contribute to the country and to public welfare without the government forcing them. If this continues year after year, what construction projects cannot be successful? How can the general public not be well-off? The ancients have already told us the principle of "teaching the people to be rich through labor." It is only because the general public cannot understand and implement it now that they always say that they cannot do anything without money. Therefore, today I would like to specifically mention it. In addition, there is one more point that I would like to add, that is, when we use the people's labor, we must allocate it properly and regulate it appropriately. We must carefully consider the location, time, and work used, and we must study the methods of management and utilization so that the people's labor will not only not be misused and wasted, but also be able to generate the greatest effect. For example, in terms of the location where the people's labor is used, it is generally based on the principle of using it in the local area. What happens in a certain place is where labor is conscripted, and where labor is conscripted is used for the benefit of that place. Only in this way can the people's labor be used most effectively, and it can also make the general public work hard without complaint. What I have said above is about striving for reality in doing things, being consistent inside and out, second, paying attention to the countryside in all political facilities, and creating welfare for the general civilians, and third, being consistent from top to bottom and helping the lack of material things with the spirit of diligence. These are the few points that I would like to contribute to everyone today, and they can also be said to be my thoughts on this trip to Wuhan. The rest of the words cannot be said all at once.

I hope that everyone can understand the meaning of what I have said today, follow the items stipulated in the Hubei Political Reorganization Outline, earnestly study them, and work together to do them. Now that we have this scale, we will definitely be able to make progress day by day in the future. I hope that Hubei can build a

A strong foundation for saving the country. I sincerely hope that everyone will work hard and wish everyone good health.

The meeting adjourned at about 10:00 AM. Chiang then met with He Chengjun, Xu Yuanquan, Shangguan Yunxiang, Liu Maoen, Liang Guanying, Hao Mengling, He Zhuguo, Wang Yizhe, Liu Duoquan, Dong Yingbin, Xia Douyin, Ye Peng, and others in the East Building. In addition, he met with Ding Bingquan and Huang Gongzhu, the deputy directors of the Security Office, and instructed them on the main points of security. He met with Hu Wenlan, Zhou Fengchi,

Luo Chunqi, Wenhua Cheng, Wen Shaohe, and Li Kuian, representatives of the Sichuan People's Anti-Bandit Support Association, and inquired about the recent situation in Sichuan Province.

He met with Xu Jizhuang, the president of the Four Provinces Farmers Bank, and inquired about the progress of business. He met with Cai Mengjian, the director of the Provincial Capital Public Security Bureau, and inquired about the public security situation. He met with Chen Jingyu, the chairman of the Hankou Chamber of Commerce, and inquired about the commercial situation in Hankou and the impact of the drought. It was not until 12:00 noon that he finished. Then, he went to the Provincial Government with Zhang Xueliang, He Chengjun, and Zhang Qun to inspect. Zhang, He, and Zhang accompanied him to the building for refreshments. He inquired Zhang Qun about the efficiency of joint office work and the terrain of the provincial capital in great detail. At 1:00 PM, he left the Provincial Government and returned to the Xingyuan via Pingyue Road and across the river. At 6:00 PM, he and his wife, Ms. Song Meiling, took a car along the river, passing Zhaogao Bureau, Longwang Temple, Zhongshan Road, and Yang Sen's Flower Garden, before returning to the Xingyuan for rest. Bandit Leader

Peng Dehuai's Confession 86

Signs of Total Collapse of Bandit Army

Nanchang Dispatch: During the Battle of Lei Bo Ridge, the National Army seized a counterfeit training order from bandit leader Peng Dehuai when it killed Zhang Sheng, the battalion commander of the pseudo-Third Division. It described the influence of the surrender and betrayal of secret information by the pseudo-officers and soldiers, as well as the disintegration of the bandit army.

It can be seen that the time for their total collapse is not far away. In order to clarify the internal truth of the bandit army for those who are concerned about suppressing bandits, we have specially extracted a few sections of the original text of the pseudo-training order as follows: (1) The corps commander (Peng Bandit's self-proclaimed title) correctly estimated the enemy's (referring to the National Army, the same below) situation on the evening of the 26th, and issued the combat order for the 27th. On the evening of the 27th, the order was supplemented by two telephone calls, stipulating that the combat preparation should be completed before 4 o'clock, and stipulating the continuous action of reconnaissance and observation posts against the enemy. However, all departments did not report on the approach of the enemy overnight. Furthermore, after the Third Battalion of the Fourteenth Regiment entered the position, they took off their equipment and went to sleep. Only four sentries were dispatched on the right flank.

The sound of the explosion of hand grenades thrown into the bunker by the enemy awakened them from their dreams. The regiment's machine guns did not enter the position at all. The regiment's second echelon was still drilling outdoors and was blocked by the enemy's artillery and air strikes and could not be reinforced. The position of the Thirty-ninth Regiment of the Thirteenth Division only had a small post, and there were no soldiers guarding it.

These serious slackness and negligence gave the enemy the opportunity to attack. Therefore, the position of the Third Battalion of the Fourteenth Regiment was closed off by the enemy without firing a shot.

The throat of the fortress, a solid fortification, was completely given to the enemy in only 30 minutes. (2) The enemy attacked from the Dalingge section where the Fourteenth Regiment and the Thirty-ninth Regiment joined.

When the Fifth Division urgently requested assistance from the Thirty-ninth Regiment, it was discovered that there was no one in the position of the Thirty-ninth Regiment at all. When Baohushan was in danger, the Second Battalion Commander of the Twelfth Regiment wanted to ask for help from the neighboring troops, but he did not know where the neighboring troops were. Baohushan had been lost for a long time, and the enemy was threatening the right flank of Wannianting, but the Thirteenth Regiment still did not know the situation on the right wing. Especially before the enemy reached the position, the assault team did not attack. (3) The enemy-surrendered members of the candle-shaped defensive team told the enemy about the candle-shaped concealed machine gun bunker and the buried landmines, so that the enemy's planes destroyed the machine gun bunker when they began to attack, and the landmines were easily destroyed by the enemy. The enemy-surrendered platoon leader of Dalingge told the enemy that the left wing of the Thirty-ninth Regiment's position was empty and that the junction's alert was weak.

Told the enemy and led the enemy to attack from this side," After our repeated encirclement and suppression, the officers and soldiers of the bandit army deeply felt the personal material suffering, and the experience of blindly following communism for several years,

Deeply knew that it was not suitable for our national conditions, and they all realized it. However, because

Under the cruel surveillance of the bandit party, there was no chance to get rid of it. Therefore, whenever the National Army advanced and approached, they carried their weapons and surrendered one after another. However, the bandit leaders were still deaf and self-righteous, and did not introspect. They blamed the failure on the slackness of the various departments of the bandit army, and wanted to use a piece of paper.

Wen, no matter how much the military's morale has been lost, deceiving oneself and others, and further exposing his desolate rubber and urging his collapse. (7th)

Luo Binghui Faction

Flees into Deep Mountains of Fujian and Jiangxi 87

丨Wang Jun Leads Troops to Tunxi丨

Wuhu Dispatch: The Luo Binghui faction, gathered a crowd of about three thousand people, and suddenly sneaked into Anhui a month ago, causing great disturbances. Various parties have sent teams to encircle and suppress them, and they have gradually disintegrated. In addition to dispatching Cai Bingyan, the director of the Security Department of the Anhui Provincial Government, to lead the Security Regiment to Tunxi for garrison, Wang Jun, the commander of the Seventh Army, was also ordered by Chairman Chiang,

Personally went to Anhui to supervise the suppression in order to completely annihilate them. Wang arrived in Wuhu by car from Beijing this afternoon. He met with representatives of the Huizhou Association in Wuhu and military and political officers. At 6:00 PM in the evening, he took a train from Xuancheng directly to Tunxi. According to Wang, the Luo bandits were severely attacked by his troops head-on in Yucun, Shicheng and other places in Huizhou, and a large number of them were killed. Even more were captured and wounded. According to the captured bandits, the role definitely killed

Two pseudo-division commanders, and now they have lost their ability to resist, so the remnants have fled back to the deep mountains on the border of Fujian and Jiangxi. The security of Huizhou,

There is no problem at all. I am going to Tunxi under orders to command the troops and track down the Qing Dynasty, so I will stay in Tunxi for no more than two weeks. (8th)

Suppressing Remaining Bandits in Chaozhou and Meizhou 88

丨Bandits Kill Village Leaders Out of Revenge丨

A dispatch from Shantou reports that the remaining bandits in the Chaozhou and Meizhou region have recently shown signs of resurgence as the main forces have moved to develop the Fujian-Jiangxi border area. Zhang Ruigui's division, stationed in Puning Liusha, and Chen Yaoshu's regiment entered Nanshan on September 27th to suppress the bandits. The first battalion encountered bandits in Xikeng, killing 14 on the spot. The remaining bandits scattered and fled into the deep mountains of Chizhuya.

The Sixth District of Chaoyang, including Shifo, Shenyang, Wai (Outer), Nei (Inner), and Ba Villages, is connected to Beishan. It is rumored that many of the bandits from Nanshan have fled into Beishan, which is located at the border of Jieyang and Puning. Therefore, Zhang's division destroyed the watchtowers in Nanyang, Wujiao, Dakeng, and other villages in Beishan. However, the bandits are now gathering on Yanquanling, Fangshan, Erfangshan, and the highest peak of Beishan (five miles from Dakeng).

At night, villagers can remotely see the bandits' flashlight beams and hear their gunshots. Moreover, bandits occasionally visit villages to give speeches and distribute reactionary propaganda songs and publications, causing great panic among the residents of more than ten nearby villages. The Houxigang port of Chaoyang faces the Shantou sea from a distance. Recently, a ship carrying seafood to Shantou was attacked by a bandit ship with weapons in front of the Qingyu Leprosarium, resulting in significant losses for the seafood merchants. The Haimenzhen Hefeng and other firms have petitioned the county government's squadron headquarters to strictly investigate and prosecute the robbers. On the 28th, the garrison in Guanbu Barracks, Chaoyang, executed six communist bandits, including Chen Yaqin, by firing squad as a warning to the public. As for the Putoubu Village in Qiupu Township, Fourth District of Chaoan County, on the 28th of last month,

it was invaded by over a hundred bandits who surrounded the residence of the village leader, Chen Yumei.

Chen, who was already asleep, was captured on the spot and shot to death.

Chen's wife, Ding, was also killed. The bandits then left with shouts and whistles. It is heard that the bandits specifically target district and village leaders for revenge because these leaders are quite capable of assisting the government in organizing and training militia to suppress bandits. Moreover, Dazhai Township in the Seventh District has also been subjected to bandit raids, causing widespread panic. The Luo Ji battalion stationed in Jinsha Township in the district believes that the district's reserve team is incompetent and should be entirely replaced with newly selected militia. On the 31st, Battalion Commander Luo went to the Dazhai Township Office and convened a security meeting attended by 26 village leaders. It was resolved that gatehouses and walls should be built in the strategic locations of the township within ten days, and each village should send ten militiamen to patrol and stand guard every night. This should be completed within three days. All firearms must also be replaced with better ones, with the village leader being responsible. Village leaders who store good firearms and fail to report them will be charged with collaborating with the bandits. All township offices and Shangguanlu Village should install telephones to facilitate communication and report bandit alerts. The

Shangguanlu Village watchtower should be reinforced with defensive works within three days and fitted with iron gatehouses within fifteen days. Watchtowers on the sides of all township offices should be constructed immediately to prepare for unforeseen events. Furthermore, County Magistrate Liang of Fengshun arrived in Shantou yesterday and stated that the remaining bandits in the mountains of Fengshun only come down to the villages at night to steal food and are not a major concern.

The bandits transferred by the Second Regiment Headquarters in Tangkeng to the county government for imprisonment include communist bandits Deng Ronghua and Liu Geng, both only thirteen years old and still wet behind the ears. They have no idea what politics and ideology are. There is an intention to release them separately. As for the female communist bandits Jian Azhen, Lan Wangshi, Lan Zhengshi, and Guan Lanshi, they are all mountain villagers who gather firewood and herd pigs and were forcibly hired by the bandits to carry goods. Although they are in prison, release is possible. On the 29th, the Third Battalion stationed in the county executed six communist bandits, including Huang Xuan, by firing squad. The Fengshun Lukou bridges, which were washed away by floods last month, have now been rebuilt. The Lengshuikeng section of the Fengliu Road has been completed, and four bridges on the Fengtang Road have also been temporarily repaired.

All roads are passable. There are some remaining bandits led by Gu Dacun in Yetian, Menxi, Hanxi, and other places. The Fifth Company of Meixian, in coordination with the Wang Minduo Battalion stationed in Fengshun, went to suppress them. On September 25th, they fought a major battle with the bandits on Menxi Mountain. The military and police charged to the mountaintop, and the bandits scattered and fled. The military and police then seized military blankets and left. (2nd)

Songjiang 89

Extortionists Sent to Court for Review

Wang Baoyuan, a resident of Xita Alley in this city, suddenly received a threatening letter demanding 300 yuan. The case was reported to the Second Precinct, and Inspector Lang, along with the detective team, ambushed and apprehended two youths, Lu Jiuxian and Yu Yaozhang, at the Release Pond. During interrogation, both denied sending the extortion letter. However, their handwriting was compared on the spot, and Yu Yaozhang's handwriting closely resembled that of the original letter. Inspector Lang was dispatched to Yu Yaozhang's home to collect evidence. Two envelopes with the inscription "Confidential, Secretariat of the Central Executive Committee of the Chinese Kuomintang" were found on his desk, matching the format of the original extortion letter. They were taken back for investigation. However, Lu Jiuxian and Wang Baoyuan are cousins on their mothers' side. Lu Jiuxian

had previously borrowed money from his aunt (Wang Baoyuan's mother) and always had his wishes granted. Now, unfortunately, he has gone astray. His aunt is kind-hearted and could not bear it. She requested the Public Security Bureau to be lenient and exempt him from investigation. However, the Public Security Bureau stated that the case involved extortion and was related to local security, and the request was denied. After recording their statements, the case was formally submitted to the County Court Prosecutor's Office for review yesterday.

Suzhou 91

Scholar Tang Jicang Receives Funeral Honors

Tang Jicang, a scholar from Huzhou, was meticulous in his conduct and

deeply learned. In his early years, he was renowned in Zhejiang and known among scholars. After coming to Shanghai, he served as a teacher at Wuben and other schools, and initiated the Huzhou Shanghai Alumni Association and the Shanghai Public School. In the late Qing Dynasty, he joined the Tongmenghui and secretly planned the revolution with martyr Chen Ying Shishi. During the restoration of Shanghai in 1911, he made significant contributions. After the establishment of the Shanghai Military Governor's Office, he served as the Secretary-General and made many contributions to municipal reforms. After the Shanghai Governor's Office was abolished, he retired to teaching and devoted himself to public service. He founded Xunyuan School, initiated the Hu Society, and served as a teacher at Nanyang Middle School. When the National Revolutionary Army vowed to launch the Northern Expedition, he traveled to Jiangxi day and night to raise funds and urged the determination of Jiangxi and Zhejiang. After returning to Shanghai, he consulted with financial leaders, encouraged them with righteousness, and spared no effort in appealing and advocating. He successively served as a member of the Shanghai Special Municipal Branch of the Chinese Kuomintang, a member of the Shanghai Provisional Political Committee, a member of the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Finance Committee, concurrently a member of the Shanghai Finance Committee, a full-time councilor of the Shanghai Special Municipal Government, the Director of the Jiangsu Provincial Polder Bureau, the Deputy Director of the State Property Management Office of the Ministry of Finance, the Director of the Zhejiang Saltpeter Bureau, and a full-time member of the Shanghai Gazetteer Compilation Office.

He also served as a councilor of the Executive Yuan and other positions. For many years, he resided in Wumen, compiling books on phonology. He occasionally went to various places to give lectures. This summer, he suddenly contracted carbuncle disease and passed away in Suzhou. The Shanghai Hu Society, the Huzhou Shanghai primary and secondary schools, and Nanyang Middle School,

held memorial services successively. The news has been reported in this newspaper. On the 7th of this month, funeral honors were received at the Longchi Ancient Temple on Gongyuan Road in Suzhou. Mourners filled the courtyard, and the event was extremely grand. The condolence couplets presented included: (Chairman Chiang) "Relying on his horse to demonstrate his talent, his fame was established early, like Chen Lin's檄 (a form of official proclamation)" "Sculpting dragons into perfect art, his phonology remains empty, like Shen Yue"

(President Dai Jitao) "Opening up the academic atmosphere of the countryside, many followers have emerged"

"Tracing the origin of our society, listening to the difficulties of the times, deeply regretting the loss of an old adult," (President Ju Zheng)

"The Hu Society dedicated grand plans, economic articles carry morality, and people think of him after his departure. Leaving behind posthumous works in Wumen, his merit and career will be passed down to future generations," (Minister Zhu Jiahua) "

Numerous writings are pushed forward, and the poetry collection of the Huzhou Society will be passed on for thousands of years." "The heavens do not spare the old, and in Wumen, a few stars suddenly fall," (Vice Minister Zeng Zhongming) "Serving as a unique military strategist, he assisted meritorious officials in achieving great achievements" "His descendants are all great talents, and his posthumous manuscripts should be hidden in famous mountains," (

Minister of Accounting and Statistics Chen) "His clear reputation is known throughout his hometown, his works are equal to his body, and his glorious career will last forever" "Thinking of the difficulties of the past, we helped each other through difficulties, and our hearts are saddened by the century-old feeling," (

Implementing Baojia and Implementing Winter Defense 92

County Magistrate Wu Qiyun, following the order of the Department of Civil Affairs, is implementing Baojia matters. He submitted it to the first district chief meeting for discussion yesterday. It was decided that it would be implemented from November 1st, in three phases: the first phase is the preparatory phase, limited to 20 days; the second phase is the Baojia compilation phase, limited to 50 days; the third phase is the household registration clearance phase, limited to 50 days. The county will select and dispatch compilation and investigation members to each district to assist the district and township mayors in handling the matter. It was also resolved to jointly form a winter defense committee with military and police agencies and district offices to implement winter defense.

Zhenjiang Customs Branch 98

Converted into an Upper and Lower Goods Office

In order to prosper the Jiangyin market, Yin Zhongren and other members of the Standing Committee of the County Chamber of Commerce submitted a request to the Customs Administration of the Ministry of Finance in April of this year, requesting that the Zhenjiang Customs Branch at the Huangtiangang Port in Beiwai be changed to a place for loading and unloading passengers and goods, and then changed to a commercial port. The Zhenjiang Customs Commissioner dispatched

Weng Changzhong to Cheng to investigate. The County Chamber of Commerce also dispatched committee members to Wujin and Wuxi counties to investigate the goods that must pass through Jiangyin for import and export, which amounted to approximately 60 million yuan. On June 11, the Chamber of Commerce convened a meeting of various agencies, and Weng

also attended. The findings were reported to the Zhenjiang Customs Commissioner and submitted to the Ministry of Finance for approval.

Now, the Customs Administration has approved the request and instructed the Chief Inspectorate to comply, and approved the prior conversion of the Jiangyin branch into a cargo station. Zhao Hansheng, the director of foreign operations of the Shanghai Young Sea Bank, heard about it and has ordered the Wuxi Wujin branch to send personnel to Cheng to contact Yin Zhongren and others, to find land in Jiangbin to prepare to build a lighter terminal and warehouse. It is expected that the Jiangyin market will prosper in the future, and the prospects are great.

Trial Opens for Case of Seducing Niece 101

Li Xiangzhi, a girl from Yuanzaogang, Nantong, is studying at a girls' middle school in Ximen, Shanghai. This year, she is 19 years old and accused her aunt, Wu Guixiang, of seducing her. Wu is currently the vice president of the Lawyers Association. Before the prosecutor's office investigated, Li returned to Nantong from Shanghai. When she arrived on Nantian Street, she was suddenly kidnapped and disappeared by Wu Guixiang's wife, Li, and Wu's secretary, Shi Zhitong. Li Xiangzhi has not arrived for several court sessions. The prosecutor asked the Criminal Court to file a separate lawsuit. The Criminal Court opened the trial on the 8th, but Li did not arrive. Her appointed agent lawyer, Shao Zhi, asked the court to immediately restore the freedom of the victim, Li Xiangzhi. The judge approved it and informed Li Xiangzhi's uncle, Li Dingyi, to be sure to bring her to the court next time.

Hangzhou

New Broadcasting Studio of Provincial Telephone Bureau Completed 102

The broadcasting studio of the Zhejiang Provincial Broadcasting Station was originally located in the Provincial Government. Due to the simple construction of the building and the lack of acoustic principles, the broadcast could not be as satisfactory as possible. The location was also unsuitable, and it was inconvenient for people from all parties to go to the station to broadcast. It is now known that the station, in order to actively reorganize, has built a new broadcasting studio on the northeast corner of the open space behind the Telephone Bureau on Huanxing Road. The construction is exquisite, and the equipment is perfect. It is divided into broadcasting studio, monitoring room, reception room, and office. The height, depth, and width of the broadcasting studio are also built according to the principles of sound, in a ratio of two, three, and five.

The broadcasting studio is also equipped with soundproof panels to prevent outside noise from entering. In addition, it is also equipped with broadcasting signal lights to indicate the actions of the broadcasting staff.

The above-mentioned new broadcasting studio was completed last month. The station has started broadcasting in the new broadcasting studio from the 1st of this month. The station also invited people from all walks of life to visit on Double Tenth Day.

Two Major Naval Constructions

Dockyard and Aircraft Factory Completed Simultaneously 113

Grand Ceremony Held Today

The Navy Department's Third Large Dockyard and the Navy Aircraft Manufacturing Plant will hold a joint completion ceremony at the same time this morning.

The details are recorded as follows:

Completion of the Third Dockyard 114

The Jiangnan Shipyard of the Navy originally had two docks. The first one is 550 feet long and the second is 402 feet long. However, these two docks are not suitable for building and repairing larger and longer ships. Years ago, the Naval Commander Chen Shaokuan,

Because of the plan to add a new No. 3 dock with deeper draft and longer capacity, the original total length was 640 feet, and the first phase is now completed, 386 feet long, 80 feet wide at the entrance, and 27 feet deep. The dock wall is made of double-layered cast iron sheet piles, with ladders on both sides leading straight to the bottom of the dock, and a slope at the end of the dock,

Prepared for transporting and unloading heavy machinery. The dock gate is also made of steel, with water tanks inside to manage the lifting and lowering of the gate. There are two water pumps, each capable of pumping 31,700 gallons per minute, and two motors, each with 380 horsepower and 720 revolutions, and a voltage of 400 volts. The above-mentioned water pumps are installed next to the dock. The newly built house is equipped with bathtubs, etc., for the use of the crew of ships entering the dock. All the equipment is extremely perfect and is truly a major construction of our country in recent years. It is also named the Third Dockyard of the Jiangnan Shipyard of the Navy. This dock has now been completed. The first phase of the project, totaling 386 feet, will hold a completion ceremony today, and the newly built Navy Yixian warship will be used by the Jiangnan Shipyard to enter the dock, in order to take the meaning of the first premier's training and construction. The project that should be expanded to the original planned 640 feet is still in progress. The Jiangnan Shipyard must clear the arsenal warehouse and the warehouse connected with the ordnance factory before starting construction. It is estimated that after the completion of the entire dock, the magnificence of the scale will not only be unmatched by the Shanghai Chinese and foreign shipyards, but also by the shipyards under the jurisdiction of China. Mr. Chen's plan this time is not only for the navy to build and repair large warships, but also for the various ship organs that should be needed in the country, such as the customs, China Merchants Bureau, salt affairs, water patrol police in various provinces,

And all the large industries, Chinese and foreign merchants, etc., are convenient. It is a relatively large construction in recent years. Today, the Navy Department sent Wu Zhennan, the director of the Coast Guard, to the dock to preside over the ceremony, and the wife of Zeng Yijing, the director of the Aircraft Division of the Jiangnan Shipyard, held the ribbon-cutting ceremony. The Jiangnan Shipyard has already sent invitations to various agencies and Chinese and foreign shipping companies to attend the ceremony at that time.

Aircraft Factory Completed Simultaneously 115

The Navy Aircraft Manufacturing Plant, because the original factory buildings were too narrow and could not meet the needs of aircraft manufacturing, Zeng Yijing, the director of the plant, specially drafted an expansion plan, which was approved by the Navy Department,

An expansion fee of 40,000 yuan was allocated. The project was tendered to Shengzaoji Construction Factory in this city to build a new aircraft assembly factory building on the open space in front of the original factory building. Construction started in April this year. The combined factory is 96 feet 10 inches wide and 121 feet deep. The house is a two-story building with a height of 25 feet on both sides and a height of 43 feet in the middle. The entire factory building is divided into sections. The middle part is used for aircraft assembly, the upper floor is used as an office, and the original factory building,

Used as a paint wood factory and tarpaulin factory. The newly built aircraft assembly factory has now been officially completed. It is scheduled to hold a completion ceremony at 10:00 a.m. today with the third new dockyard. Chen Zaofan will execute the completion ceremony, and the factory will start working from that day.

5

Development of Commercial Aviation 117

Dai Enji, the general manager of China National Aviation Corporation, yesterday presented a general overview of the development of commercial aviation in China in the past five years, saying that people from all countries have always considered our country's transportation industry to be extremely naive. The source of this concept is actually because our country's railways are not very developed, and everyone thinks that building railways is the most important issue in building our country's transportation industry. However, everyone knows that our country has relied on the benefits of Tianhe waterway transportation since ancient times. Improving this waterway will be of great benefit to preventing various water and drought disasters. Moreover, judging from the production of various provinces, most of the provinces can close their borders and be self-sufficient. Therefore, although there is a lack of railways, it is not so difficult. However, our country's territory is almost the same as the entire Europe. If we want to build railways throughout the country, the huge cost required may not be borne by the country for a while. What our country currently needs is not ordinary railways, but a more convenient and economical transportation tool than railways, which can increase the special speed for the transportation of mail and goods and the travel of passengers, in order to make up for the shortcomings of waterway transportation, and will not consume huge resources to increase the burden on the country and the people. There are two tools: highways and aviation. The effect of highway construction is actually twice the result with half the effort compared to railways. All goods transportation and ordinary travel across the country are convenient. As for aviation, its efficiency has been recognized by the world. If waterway, highway, and aviation transportation can be used at the same time, then our country's transportation problem can be completely solved. At the beginning of the establishment of the National Government, Sun Ke, the Minister of Railways, realized this, and signed a contract with the US Aviation Development Company to establish China National Aviation Corporation in order to promote air transportation. At that time, there were slight setbacks, but it was still able to work hard to achieve its success. This is the beginning of the development of our country's aviation industry. At the beginning of the establishment of China National Aviation Corporation,

There were many difficulties in the arrangement of everything. For example, the lease of various aircraft fields and their equipment, the investigation and research of climate changes in various places, and the training of radio telegraphers and clerks at each station, etc.

It is enough to cause setbacks. The day of the beginning of preparations was July 8th, the 18th year of the Republic of China. By October 20th, everything was ready. On this day, a Lockheed aircraft was used to make the first official flight between Shanghai and Hankou. The stations in the middle were Nanjing, Anqing, and Jiujiang. The distance was 516 miles. This is the general situation of the establishment of the aviation line in the lower reaches of the Yangtze River. On April 1st, the 20th year of the Republic of China, the Shanghai-Hankou route was extended to Yichang. On October 11th of the same year, it was extended from Yichang to Chongqing. The entire route from Shanghai to Chongqing totaled more than 1,600 miles. The stations along the route are all commercial centers in the Yangtze River Basin. After the Hankou-Chongqing route was opened to traffic, preparations were immediately made for the Beiping route. This route officially started flying on January 10th, the 22nd year of the Republic of China, stopping along the way in Haizhou, Qingdao, and Tianjin. The success of this route is entirely due to the urging and economic assistance of Zhu Jia-hua, the Minister of Transportation, so that the company would not suffer a major economic loss when opening this route. On October 24th of the same year, the Shanghai-Guangdong route was also officially opened, passing through Wenzhou, Fuzhou, Xiamen, and Shantou. This route connects the three basins of the Yellow River, the Yangtze River, and the Pearl River, so that important cities across the country can communicate with each other. On November 11th of the same year, thanks to the efforts of Minister Zhu, the Chongqing-Chengdu route was established. By this time, Chengdu, the richest city in Sichuan, was also connected to Shanghai.

Equipment and flights: The aircraft used on the Shanghai-Chongqing route are Lockheed amphibious aircraft, which can carry one pilot, one co-pilot, and four passengers, with a speed of 90 miles per hour. There is one flight back and forth between Shanghai and Hankou every day, and three flights back and forth between Hankou and Chongqing every week. The aircraft flying on the Shanghai-Beiping and Chongqing-Chengdu routes are Stinson land-based aircraft, which can carry one pilot, one co-pilot, and four passengers, with a speed of 110 miles per hour. There are three flights back and forth between Shanghai and Beiping every week, and four flights back and forth between Chongqing and Chengdu every week. The Shanghai-Guangdong route will use Douglas Daerfang amphibious aircraft from October 15th of this year. This aircraft can carry one pilot and one co-pilot each, as well as eight passengers, with a speed of 150 miles per hour.

Pilots: The pilots hired by the company are strictly selected,

Have received special training, so they are rich in commercial aviation experience. This is not easily achieved by any country's airline. Currently, 12 pilots and 12 co-pilots have been hired, including 11 Americans, 1 German, and 11 Chinese.

Future expansion plan: Recently, the company's business development has seen rapid progress, which shows that air transportation is in urgent need in the society. In order to meet this need, a future plan has been formulated to develop our country's aviation industry. The main points are as follows:

Shanghai-Hankou route: It is planned to replace the existing Lockheed aircraft with two Fairchild amphibious aircraft with 700 horsepower. The aircraft has a speed of 160 miles per hour and can carry two pilots and eight passengers.

It is also planned to change the flights from one flight back and forth every day to two flights back and forth every day.

Hankou-Chongqing route: It is also planned to replace the existing Lockheed aircraft with Fairchild aircraft, and it is planned to change from three flights back and forth every week to one flight back and forth every day.

Shanghai-Beiping route: The Stinson aircraft currently used on this route will also be

Replaced by a new type of Lockeheed variable engine aircraft. The speed per hour is 200 miles, and it can carry one pilot and ten passengers.

It is planned to change the number of flights from three times a week to one time a day. Chongqing-Kunming route: Yunnan's transportation relies solely on the Dian-Yue Railway. If you travel from Chongqing to Kunming, the only means of transportation is mostly carrying shoulders and walking on sheep intestines trails, crossing mountains and ridges. It takes 12 days to reach Guiyang, and another 12 days to reach Kunming. It is now planned to open a Chongqing-Kunming route in the shortest possible time. It takes one and a half hours to fly from Chongqing to Guiyang, and another one and a half hours,

That is, it reaches Kunming. Therefore, the arduous journey that takes 24 days can be completed in three hours.

Radio equipment: The company has radio stations at each station and backup airport. The Douglas Daerfang aircraft used on the Shanghai-Guangdong route last month, and the Lockeheed and Fairchild aircraft planned to be used on the Shanghai-Beiping and Shanghai-Chengdu routes are all equipped with radio equipment, which can communicate with land stations at any time during the flight.

The company suffered heavy losses at the beginning of its establishment. This situation is unavoidable for airlines in all countries. What is gratifying is that the company's business report on June 30th this year, apart from depreciation, has a slight surplus. This achievement is enough to break the records of famous airlines around the world, because the company has not received government subsidies, and this result is unique. The company's directors, in view of this excellent result, plan to purchase the latest equipment mentioned above with a huge amount of more than one million yuan, in order to achieve the purpose of expanding business and serving the people.

Nine Months of This Year

Shanghai Exports to the United States 118

Slight Increase Over the Same Period Last Year

An evening newspaper in the United States said that according to statistics recently released by the US Consulate General in Shanghai, the total value of Shanghai's exports to the United States in the first nine months of this year was US$8,572,296, an increase of more than one million yuan compared with the total value of US$7,317,341 in the same period last year. Shanghai's exports to the United States in September accounted for US$642,390, of which the increase in inedible animals and animal products was the largest, with a total value of US$2,787,926 in the first nine months of last year, and the total value in the first nine months of this year jumped to US$4,149,376. The second largest was textiles, followed by inedible plant products.

The products that saw a decrease were edible animals and animal products and minerals. In the first nine months of this year, Shanghai's exports to the Philippines

The total value of the Philippines was US$955,104, an increase compared with US$878,852 in the same period last year, but exports to Hawaii decreased slightly.

Negotiated in detail,

Qin Xitian and Others Petitioned the Ministry of Finance

Thorough Investigation of Tax Police Harassing the People 123

Accusing Good People of Being Smugglers

Identifying Pickled Vegetables as Prohibited Items

Shanghai County citizen Qin Xitian and others specially jointly petitioned Minister of Finance Kong Xiangxi regarding the tax police harassing the people. The text reads: A petition for the tax police to violate the law and harm the people. Please investigate thoroughly and severely punish them to stabilize the local area and rectify discipline. Shanghai County's second district borders Huangpu and does not produce salt. Residents all make a living by farming. On September 2nd of this year, a boat was robbed in the port. The owner followed the trace ashore and shouted for villagers to catch two thieves and send them to the county. The gang of thieves harbored resentment, so at midnight on the 4th, they gathered 30 to 40 people, each armed with guns, and robbed four families in a row. The villagers were terrified and guarded each other. In the evening of the 8th, there were also four people dressed in plain clothes and carrying cloth bags on their backs, wandering around looking suspicious. The villagers went to interrogate them, but those people took out the guns they were carrying on their backs and shot at people.

The villagers rose up to resist, injuring one person in the brawl and capturing three people, along with the guns, and sending them to the Shanghai County Public Security Bureau. Later, the tax police captain filed a complaint with the Shanghai District Court. The court immediately subpoenaed witnesses for investigation. On the morning of the 21st, dozens of armed men suddenly took a boat from Pudong to the district and raided in teams. A total of eight families were destroyed with doors, windows, and utensils, and robbed of gold and silver jewelry. Ten people were kidnapped. Several days later, four of them took the opportunity to escape back and claimed that they had been dragged off the boat by the police and taken to Dujiaxing Town in Nanhui County, where they were detained at the police headquarters. They were repeatedly subjected to private torture and beatings, forcing them to confess to salt smuggling, resulting in injuries all over their bodies. The whereabouts of the other six people are unknown. Therefore, the villagers were afraid of their return, abandoned their fields and houses, and fled one after another. On the 26th, when the court summoned them, Li Youlian, the head of the district, learned that the six kidnapped people had been sent to the court by the police. The court ordered Li District Head to find bail and release them. The case has not yet been closed. It is found that the Shanghai newspapers on December 23rd, 22nd year of the Republic of China, carried a Nanjing special telegram with a notice from Junbu that in the future, the tax police organs in each district, if the tax police detect that civilian households and shops are harboring smuggled salt, they must search, and they can first send police to guard outside,

At the same time, tax police wearing uniforms should cooperate with the local authorities to handle the matter in accordance with the law, and must not arbitrarily enter and search in order to maintain police discipline and avoid incidents. Those who violate this will be severely punished, etc. The Ministry of Finance's earnest intention to rectify discipline and maintain public order, but the tax police in each district often use the name of searching to intimidate and defraud the weak, plunder property, and even plant evidence to extort ransoms, accusing good people of being smugglers and identifying pickled vegetables and pickles as prohibited items. They act like tigers and foxes and run rampant everywhere. Our people are occasionally angered by them, and they are subjected to severe torture and heavy fines, causing them to be crippled, their families ruined, and their grievances unanswered. For example, in the case of the second district, because the villagers were repeatedly robbed, questioning pedestrians was still a legitimate defense. Why didn't the tax police report the incident, and immediately used their wild methods, which led to a fatal case. When the lawsuit was filed with the court, why didn't they wait for the court to handle it, and dared to openly rob, arrest civilians, use private torture, and illegally imprison them in broad daylight with armed ammunition,

Such trampling on civil rights, violating Jun orders, harming the political system, and not benefiting tax revenue,

If it is not thoroughly investigated and severely punished, how can the local area be stabilized and military discipline rectified? The commanders of the responsible district teams, who allow their subordinates to run rampant and do not prohibit them, are also difficult to excuse.

In order to dare to ask Junbu to select honest and just officials, go to the scene of the incident, conduct a thorough investigation, and give each a corresponding punishment, so that they can eliminate evil and appease the good in order to live up to Junbu's admonitions to the tax police. For the sake of public gratitude, I respectfully present to Minister of Finance Kong, The person who filed the report is Qin Xitian, a citizen of Shanghai County, Jiangsu Province (

74 years old, residing in the fifth district of Shanghai County, co-signed by Jin Qingzhang, Qiao Tang, Ding Jicheng, Kang Yongnian, Kong Xiangbai, Niu Changkang, Shi Qiguang, Gu Wenjun, Cai Yan, Ren Yongkang,

Not Joining the Guild

Still Liable for Membership Obligations 124

The Ministry of Industry and Commerce Replied to the City Chamber of Commerce

The Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce previously stated that the failure of merchants in various industries to join the industry guild hindered the sound organization of the group, and had repeatedly requested the government to determine the sanctions for industries that do not join the industry guild. The situation was previously published in the newspaper. It is now learned that the association recently received a reply from the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, saying, "Both reports are known. Regarding the case of industries not joining the guild, the Central People's Movement Committee and the Hubei Provincial Government have recently transferred the consultation, according to which the Hankou City Chamber of Commerce requested that clear methods be stipulated to force industries to join the guild uniformly, and that for merchants who do not join the association,

They should be held equally liable for all the obligations of members, etc. It should be based on Article 3, Paragraph 2, Article 4, Paragraph 1, and Article 7 of the Industry and Commerce Guild Law. The members of the industry guild are the companies and firms of all industries in the local area. All industries should naturally join the guild, fulfill the obligations of members, and abide by the rules of association. There is no freedom to withdraw or not join the association except for those who are suspended, relocated, or removed from the association. The so-called joining the association in Article 4, Paragraph 2, Item 5 of the same law refers to the regulations for joining the association. If a merchant is negligent in fulfilling the procedures for joining the association, it cannot be exempted from its obligations.

The association's proposal to hold merchants who do not join the association equally liable for all the obligations of members is in accordance with the laws and regulations. The most important obligation of members is to pay membership dues. For those who do not fulfill this obligation, the interpretation of the Judicial Yuan on May of last year, No. 914, can be applied and used for payment in accordance with the law, etc." I hereby reply to your knowledge, and it is necessary to inform you of this approval.

Qian Chengxu Returned Home and Talked 125

Europe's Light Industry Is Exceptionally Developed

To Save the Countryside, Production Should Be Promoted

According to the National Society, Qian Chengxu, PhD, the secretary-general of the Municipal Industrial Federation, attended the International Labor Conference on behalf of our country. After the conference closed, he stayed in Europe for a long time and traveled to various countries to inspect industry. His footprints covered the entire Europe. Now Mr. Qian has returned home. The reporter specially went to inquire yesterday and was told about the journey.

Foreign Impressions 126

Mr. Qian stated that his recent trip to Europe to attend the International Labour Conference, after several years of absence, revealed a changed European landscape. Although Europe is affected by the economic downturn, with a sharp increase in unemployed workers, causing social and economic panic, Europeans are now

devoting themselves to the cause of production, hoping to overcome the current difficulties.

Consequently, emerging light industries are exceptionally developed, with numerous inventions of light industrial machinery. These machines occupy less space and are cheaper, making them extremely common. He has compiled two books based on his observations: one is "An Economic Atlas of Europe,"

which uses diagrams to illustrate European economic relationships, and the other is "A Report on Industrial Investigation in Europe," which provides a very detailed account of European industry, totaling over a million words.

Return Plan 127

Mr. Qian further told the reporter that China has suffered from the global economic panic externally and frequent disasters internally in recent years, leading to the increasing bankruptcy of the rural economy. He believes that there is no alternative but to devote ourselves to production. He is now planning to gather like-minded people to establish a light industry manufacturing company, initially setting up a flour mill. This type of factory requires very little capital and yields significant benefits. If people across the country can emulate its establishment, it will greatly benefit the people's livelihood.
