British Revised Import Duty on Silk 132

According to news from the Guidance Division of the International Trade Bureau, after the revision of the new British-French commercial treaty, the United Kingdom has implemented revised tariffs on natural silk, artificial silk, and goods made entirely or partially of natural silk or artificial silk from July 2 this year. Among them, raw silk, artificial silk, etc. have been reduced separately,

then China can enjoy the same treatment under the most-favored-nation clause. The silk tariff rates in the commercial treaty are translated below, and silk exporters are requested to pay attention to them (there may be errors in the translation, the original English version shall prevail): Silk and artificial silk tariffs, silk and artificial silk, and goods made entirely or partly of silk or artificial silk, shall be taxed according to the tariff rates specified in this section. Goods in the following sections one and two shall be taxed according to tariff rates in section two and three respectively."

Section 1. (1) Silk (unit: pound) (A) Silk waste and silk noils, unbleached, six pence; bleached in whole or in part (excluding short-fiber waste silk), one shilling and six pence; short-fiber waste silk, six pence;

(B) Raw silk, unbleached, one shilling and six pence; bleached in whole or in part, two shillings and two pence; (C) Silk yarn, 25 percent ad valorem, unbleached, two shillings, pence per pound; bleached in whole or in part, (excluding spun silk) two shillings and nine pence; spun silk, nine pence; (2)

Silk fabrics, (refer to Note A) (A) Pure pongee (unbleached) two shillings and three pence per pound; (B) Spun silk fabrics, ten pence, 25 percent ad valorem; (C) Other fabrics (excluding Shandong, Ninghai, Nanshan, Henan, Andong, Habutai and other oriental silk fabrics),

25 percent ad valorem, in quantity, unbleached, two shillings and three pence per pound; bleached in whole or in part, three shillings and six pence. (If the warp or weft of these fabrics is bleached in whole or in part, a tax of three shillings and six pence per pound shall be levied; if unbleached, a tax of two shillings and

three pence shall be levied.) (3) Artificial silk, A. Waste silk, nine pence per pound, B.

Silk yarn, one shilling and three pence per pound, 25 percent ad valorem, C. Fabrics (refer to Note A) one shilling and five pence per pound, 25 percent ad valorem, Note A···A Goods woven with a part of silk or artificial silk, in which the weight of silk or artificial silk, or the sum of silk and artificial silk, does not exceed 10% of the total weight of the fabric, shall be taxed at 20% of the total value of the goods. B Goods woven with all or part of silk, (this is all or part (bleached but not waste) or artificial silk, the width of which exceeds twelve inches, in which the weight of silk or artificial silk, and the sum of artificial silk, is more than 75%, the tariff rules are as follows: One, silk woven goods shall be taxed at seven and a half pence per square yard (calculated according to the area of the fabric) or 25% ad valorem; Two, artificial silk woven goods shall be taxed at five pence per square yard (calculated according to the area of the fabric) or 25% ad valorem.

Section 2 (1) Shandong, Ninghai (Nanshan, Henan, Andong, Habutai, and other oriental silk goods, A. Dyed and printed types, three shillings and six pence per pound, seven and a half pence per square yard, or 25% ad valorem; B. Undyed and printed types, two shillings and nine pence per pound, 25% ad valorem.

Section 3 Other goods, excluding books, the silk or artificial silk content of which is in paper in knots, or in bindings, clothing, fabrics, bedding (quilts, bed curtains, mattresses, sheets, pillowcases, mattress covers,

clothing, and similar goods), various curtains, cushion covers, chair covers, tablecloths, table mats, table center cloths, table edge round cloth cushions, finger bowls, crepe,

and similar goods, (goods made entirely of silk, or artificial silk fabrics, or containing silk or artificial silk ingredients, or the sum of the two ingredients, the value of which exceeds 20% of the total value of the goods), goods containing silk ingredients, 43 and one-third percent ad valorem, or twelve shillings per pound; goods not containing silk ingredients, 43 and one-third percent ad valorem, or five shillings per pound, (1) (the value of silk or artificial silk ingredients, or the sum of the two ingredients, exceeding 5% but not exceeding 20% of the total value of the goods), goods containing silk ingredients, 25% ad valorem, or four shillings per pound, goods not containing silk ingredients, 25% ad valorem, or, shillings per pound, (3) silk or artificial silk ingredients, or the sum of the two ingredients, the value of which does not exceed 5% of the total value of the goods, goods containing silk ingredients, 12% ad valorem, or nine pence per pound, goods not containing silk ingredients, 12% ad valorem, or four pence per pound.

Then, the disaster has already formed, and the autumn harvest is hopeless, resulting in many houses being empty, and mournful cries everywhere. There are even those who do not have enough food and starve to death, and those who have built up debt and commit suicide out of despair. As for the looting of rice, it is even more common. In a blink of an eye, the severe winter is approaching, and millions of disaster victims have no food to eat or clothes to keep warm.

Mortgages are empty, and borrowing is impossible. If relief is not provided quickly, they will either die of starvation or freeze to death. Bandits are lurking in all four townships,

always thinking about moving. The future of public security should be prevented in advance. Disaster relief and security are matters that cannot be delayed. Wang Pengzhou, a 50-year-old man from Yuyao, who sells foreign socks, lives in Yucang Street,

In the city, a man named Chen Qifa from Taizhou, about 34 years old, living at No. 90 Yuli, took a box of gauze silk stockings from Wang a week ago. At that time, he issued a banknote of ten yuan as a mortgage to Wang. Afterwards, Wang used the banknote, and the smoke exchange store said it was counterfeit and asked Wang where he got it from. Wang went to look for Chen Qifa, but Chen denied it. Wang was furious and lit a cigarette. He accidentally burned a cigarette case belonging to Chen. Chen immediately negotiated with Wang because there was a pawn ticket in the burned cigarette case, which was a diamond ring, which was also burned. He wanted Wang to compensate for the loss. Because of the dispute, police officer Wang Yaozong from the post arrived and detained both of them at the Laobeimen Police Station for investigation. According to Chief Shen's interrogation, Wang Pengzhou Chen Qifa used counterfeit banknotes and negotiated with him. According to Chen Qifa, Wang Pengzhou burned my cigarette case, which contained valuable pawn tickets, and wanted to shirk responsibility and deliberately falsely accused me of using counterfeit banknotes. As the case is related to the use of counterfeit banknotes and fraud, although the statements of both parties are contradictory, they will be handed over to the court for interrogation.

Another Theft Case in the Second District of the County 143

Two Households Robbed in One Night, The Victim Suffered Injury

In the territory of the Second District of Shanghai County, theft cases have occurred frequently recently. Around 11:00 pm the night before last, more than a dozen bandits came to Sunjiazhai, Guantao Township in the district. They were all armed and broke into the homes of residents Sun Shuxiang and Sun Tusheng. The victims were awakened from their sleep. The bandits first tied up the men, women, old, and young and placed them in a corner, forbidding them to make a sound. Then they rummaged through the boxes and cabinets and searched wantonly. The silver dollars, clothes, and chickens and ducks robbed from the two families totaled hundreds of gold in losses. The search lasted about two hours before they let out a shout and fled south with their loot.

When the bandits were searching, Zhang, the mother of the victim Sun Tusheng, was beaten severely and suffered serious head injuries for shouting at the bandits. She is now groaning in bed, and her life is worrying. The victim has reported the incident to the Tangwan Public Security Sub-station for investigation, and it has been forwarded to the Public Security Bureau for verification.

Zhu Hailiang Commits Suicide Due to Poverty 144

Zhu Hailiang, a 49-year-old man from Anhui, lived in a hut at Gaolang Bridge, Yangshupu Lan Road. Yesterday morning, at about 10:00, due to economic pressure and no way out, he had the idea of committing suicide. He then committed suicide by hanging himself in the room.

Afterwards, the Yulin Road Police Station sent Chinese police officer No. 242 to the scene. The body was transported to the Tongren Hospital for examination at the autopsy room.

Dixiwei Road

Erroneous Jurisdiction in the Red Pill Case 145

Should be Transferred to the District Court for Trial

The Chinese and Western detectives of the Tsz Wei Road Police Station discovered a red pill drug manufacturing operation on the 15th of last month at around 4 PM, inside a house at 59 Route Say Zoong, confiscating a large quantity of morphine, heroin, and other materials, as well as machine parts. They arrested three workers on the spot: Wang Asan from Wuxi, Zhang Asan from the local area, and Hang Xiqing from Ningbo. Hang attempted to escape by jumping out the window, injuring himself, and was sent to the hospital for treatment. The next morning, Wang and Zhang were sent to the First Special District Court for questioning. It was revealed that the operation was established by a Japanese man named Ikeda, and police detectives subsequently arrested a Japanese man named Gai Li and sent him to the Japanese Consulate for investigation.

Orders were given for the two defendants to be remanded in custody, pending Hang Xiqing's recovery from his injuries and further interrogation. Yesterday morning, Hang recovered and, along with Wang and Zhang, was sent to the Third Criminal Court.

The Shanghai Municipal Council lawyer, Li Zhishan, stated that according to the Japanese side's testimony, two Chinese shareholders named Lu and Shen were at large. The police station filed a public prosecution under Article 6 of the Opium Suppression Law, requesting severe punishment according to the law. Judge Xiao briefly questioned the defendants and, due to the case being under incorrect jurisdiction, ordered the case to be transferred to the Shanghai District Court for trial. Lawyer Li stated that during the appeal period, the defendants should remain in custody, which the court approved.

Extortion Case

Ji Zhongming Found Not Guilty 146

Tang Naixiu, a Cantonese resident at 246 Route Lyonne, recently received multiple threatening letters from bandits, demanding 500 yuan.

Initially, a negotiation was arranged at the Taikoo Wharf in the French Concession, but it was ignored. Then, another meeting was set near 451 Jiangxi Road, instructing to throw the money into a drain, where someone would retrieve it. Tang reported it to the Tsz Wei Road Police Station, who dispatched Detective Chief Fan De Fu,

Detective Liu Decheng, and others. On the 1st of this month, they prepared five-yuan and one-yuan notes of Zhejiang Industrial Bank, mixed with ghost money, and went to the designated location and threw the package into the drain. After waiting for a while, there was no sign of anyone taking it. The detectives found a hole connecting to the house at 455, and inside, they apprehended Ji Zhongming from Haimen, who was highly suspected. He used to work as a tea server at Tang's place and resigned for unknown reasons. He was arrested and taken to the police station. He claimed that the incident was his father's doing and was sent to the First Special District Court. His testimony was evasive, and he was remanded in custody. Yesterday morning, Judge Su Xiebin presided over a further hearing in the Third Criminal Court. When questioned about his confession at the police station, he stated that admitting it was his father who took the package and other statements were made under duress. He claimed he had no grievances against Tang, and his father was in his hometown and had not come to Shanghai, requesting the court's understanding. Judge Xiao Xiebin found the evidence insufficient and declared Ji Zhongming not guilty.

The Shanghai Municipal Council lawyer, Li Zhishan, requested remand in custody pending appeal, which the court granted.

Abridged Translations of Various Essays on Sino-Japanese Issues

The "Newsletter," a monthly publication of the International Problems Research Association, primarily features abridged translations of articles from foreign magazines, with the aim of introducing general world opinions. There is also an article titled "The Investments of the Great Powers in North China," which is an abridged translation from a Japanese economic journal. It is feared that our countrymen may not be fully aware of this. The "Newsletter" is not for sale and, in addition to being distributed to members, the association will distribute it to important institutions, organizations, schools, and libraries both domestically and internationally.

Altered Lottery Ticket Judgement 148

丨Qian Changyu Sentenced to One Year and Six Months丨

Qian Changyu, from Wuxi, a 22-year-old accountant at the Xinhu Socks Factory at 4 Jin Tong Village, Xujiahui Road, in the French Concession, took two seventh-period aviation lottery tickets, numbers 323499 and 364099, to the Shengchang Cigarette and Paper Shop at the south end of the Great World on the afternoon of the 28th of last month to redeem them. The shop clerk, Qian Zongying, discovered that the last digit of both tickets had been altered. He detained the person and the tickets and reported it to the Lottery Office.

An official, Zhao Chisin, was sent to verify the tickets, and Qian was sent to the French police station. The police lawyer prosecuted him for fraud and forging documents. Judge Li Changnian conducted a preliminary hearing, and details were previously reported. The case has now concluded, and yesterday morning, Judge Li presided over the First Criminal Court, handing down the verdict: Qian Changyu, intending to use altered valuable lottery tickets, was sentenced to one year and six months of imprisonment. The number of days he was detained before the verdict was finalized will be counted at a rate of two days of detention for one day of imprisonment. The two forged tickets were confiscated. During the appeal period, the defendant will be remanded in custody at the detention center.

Apprentice

Suicidal After Being Reprimanded for Gambling 150

Bo Xi, a young man from Hubei, 19 years old, was introduced by his uncle, Guo Naishan (54 years old, from Tianjin, currently residing at 8 Xideli, Route Paul Henry, in the French Concession, working as a customs broker), to learn the customs brokerage business at the Yu Yansheng Customs Brokerage at 6 Xiangxing Lane, 91 Route de la Grande Armée, a year and a half ago. Recently, his behavior changed; he became lazy at work,

and focused solely on gambling. Last Saturday and Sunday, he did not complete the unified tax certification form and gambled with the drivers at night. On Sunday, the manager, Zhou Wenqing (40 years old, from Ningbo), found out and reprimanded him. The young Liao, in a fit of anger, felt he had nowhere to vent his frustration and became despondent. That afternoon at 4 PM, he bought two large boxes of raw opium and, at 10 PM, returned to the brokerage, went to bed, and swallowed it, committing suicide. At 9 AM on the 8th, his colleagues noticed that he had not gotten up. They called him, but he did not respond. When they lifted the covers, they found Liao dead in bed. They immediately informed the manager and reported it to the police station. Detectives were sent to investigate, and the body was taken to the Tongren Fuyuan branch for an autopsy. The deceased's parents are still in his hometown of Wuchang. His uncle telegraphed them to inform them. Yesterday, the police station reported to the First Special District Court, which appointed Prosecutor Wang Ren, along with a forensic doctor and recorder, to examine the body. They questioned the deceased's uncle, Guo Naishan, the manager, Zhou Wenqing, and witness He Yumin,

concluding that Liao Bo Xi had indeed died from swallowing raw opium. The body was released to Guo Naishan and others for burial. A small amount of opium was stored in the warehouse.

Convening Motion 157

The Child Welfare Association has been established for six years,

striving for the well-being of children through methods such as protection, security, and relief, with education and relief complementing each other. Although it may not be perfect, it has a basic structure. Recently, the Association has further sought the development of child welfare work, so that the organization of child welfare groups across the country

can gradually become unified in an orderly manner. The key question is how to seek appropriate connections, how to develop concrete education plans, how to adapt to the psychology and physiology of children, and how to meet the needs of the social environment. Furthermore, in response to the national government's clear directive,

which designates 1935 as Children's Year, how should preparations be made to promote this great movement nationwide? All of these issues

require the gathering of contemporary child welfare leaders and experts in child education, hygiene, and psychology to jointly explore solutions, in order to form a comprehensive approach and promote the advancement of the work.

JinCheng Bank

Investing in Rural North China 161

Providing Small Loans to Regulate the Farmers' Economy

Cotton Production Cooperation and Transportation Have Been Quite Effective

In recent years, China's rural economy has been utterly ruined, and the lives of farmers have been arduous, urgently requiring relief. Banks in this city are investing in rural areas to regulate the rural

economy, in order to restore their original prosperity. Recently, JinCheng Bank has jointly established the North China Agricultural Improvement Association with the Ding County of Hebei Province and the Mass

Education Promotion Association, with the goal of developing cotton production in Ding County. Recently, they also plan to invest funds. Details are as follows:

Cotton Production Transportation Quite Effective 162

This year, JinCheng Bank of this city, together with the Ding County of Hebei Province, the Mass Education Promotion Association, and the Economic Research Institute of Nankai University, jointly established a North China Agricultural Improvement Society. Its business operations involve transportation cooperation. According to the original cotton-producing area of Ding County, it can produce 300,000 dan of cotton annually, worth approximately 30 million yuan. Previously, the transportation cost per dan of cotton and the commissions earned by middlemen required about 7 to 9 yuan. Now, after the bank and the Livelihood Department of the Mass Education Promotion Association have cooperated in transportation, the transportation cost per dan of cotton is only 2.5 yuan.

Investing Two Hundred Thousand in Rural Loans 163

It is also reported that after the bank cooperated with the local Mass Education Society to carry out rural undertakings, remarkable results have been achieved.

There is very little risk in lending to rural areas, so it is planned to temporarily invest 200,000 yuan this year. If good results are obtained in the future, it is planned to increase the investment amount. As for the investment policy, it is said that it will focus on small loans, with most requiring reliable collateral. The various regulations that have been formulated are extremely strict, and progress has been quite smooth in recent days.

Hongkou Xiangyan Bridge

Trial of Homicide Case Opens 164

Caused by Borrowing an Opium Pipe, Resulting in Tragedy

The Deceased Was an Only Child, His Father Has No One to Rely On

At the entrance of Juxing Lane, Xiangyan Bridge, Hongkou, at around 10 PM on the night of September 4th, a melee occurred, and a stray bullet struck the abdomen of Liu Jinfa, who worked at the Huasi Cloth Factory at No. 22 in the lane. He was immediately

sent to Tongren Hospital, where he died despite treatment. Afterward, the Linping Road Police Station arrested Sun Jieshou (also known as Sun Laosan), who fired the shot, and transferred him to the District Court, where he was interrogated and detained pending

investigation. The details were previously reported. As for the cause of this case, it is said that Xie Arong, a resident of the kitchen shed at No. 25 Juxing Lane, and

Ji Laosan, who lived in the nearby Xiangshan Lane, both privately operated opium dens, providing opium for people to smoke. Xie and Ji were also close friends. One day, Xie Arong's opium had run out, and his customers were impatiently waiting. Therefore, Xie went to Ji Laosan's house to borrow four opium pipes. Ji's wife instructed Xie to take five opium pipes from the opium jar himself. The next day, Xie only returned four pipes. Ji's wife immediately questioned Xie as to why he had returned one less pipe. Xie refused to accept this, which led to a conflict. Both sides invited many people to engage in a melee, resulting in a fatality. Now, the case has been preliminarily investigated by Prosecutor Kong Xianglin, who has filed a charge of homicide with the Criminal Court. Yesterday afternoon at 3 PM, Judge Zhang Shao specially opened the Fifth Court for the trial, ordering the prisoner, Sun Jieshou (also known as Sun Laosan), to be brought to the case. He stated that he was 23 years old, a Shanghainese, residing at No. 1, Lane 77, Taiping Bridge Road, and working as a supervisor at the Mingsheng Smelting Factory. When asked, "Do you know Zhu Laosan?" he replied, "I don't recognize him." When asked,

"Why did you fight on the night of the 4th of last month?" he replied, "I don't know. At that time, I was still working at the factory and had not yet left work." When asked, "Did you shoot Liu Jinfa, causing his death?" he replied, "That is not true." When asked, "When were you arrested?" he replied, "I was arrested at home around 12 AM that night." When asked, "Before the deceased died, he said in the hospital that Sun Laosan definitely fired the shot and that he was a big man. Furthermore, the prosecutor from this court said that you fired the shot when he examined the injury in the hospital. Where is the handgun now?" he replied, "I am a businessman, how would I have a handgun?" The official ordered the witness, Zhu Laosan, to be brought to the case. He stated that he was 29 years old, from Xinghua, residing in Xiangshan Lane, Wuhua Road, and working as a laborer at an egg factory. On the 4th of last month, Xie Arong came to my house and called me outside, accusing me of reporting his privately operated opium den to the police,

saying that I was the one who reported it. Therefore, Xie, along with Sun Jieshou (also known as Sun Laosan) and three or four others, made trouble for me. Because I saw Sun Laosan holding a handgun, I was extremely frightened and fled, and then I heard a gunshot. When asked, "Have you known Sun Laosan for a long time?" he replied,

"I recognize him." Next, according to Zhang Liu, 36 years old, from Hangzhou, residing at No. 22 Juxing Lane, Xiangyan Bridge, and working at the Huasi Cloth Factory, the deceased, Liu Jinfa, was an apprentice of my husband, Zhang Yulin. On the night of the shooting, I was not at home. It is said that Liu Jinfa and my six-year-old son were watching a small book under the electric light at the door when this tragedy occurred. When I returned home and learned of it, I telegraphed the deceased's father, Liu Liansheng, to come to Shanghai. When asked, "Do you recognize Sun Laosan?" she replied, "I don't recognize him." Finally, according to Liu Liansheng, 54 years old, from Xiaoshan, my son, Liu Jinfa, died tragically for no reason, but I only had one son, and I will have no one to rely on in the future.

I request justice. The judge said, "If you have a request, you should formally file a petition. There is still a need to investigate this case, so we will continue the hearing later." He was returned to custody.

Mother Returned Home Late at Night

Daughter Had Already Burned to Death 165

Fire at Home, No One to Rescue the Girl

Regret After the Fact, How Could the Deceased Come Back to Life?

Chen Du, a woman from Nanhui, residing in the front building at No. 33, Yongshou Lane, 584 Route Joffre, in the French Concession, 33 years old, told her six-year-old daughter, Jin Di, to

go to bed first the night before last. She then took her young son out for a stroll, not returning until late at night. Unexpectedly, at 1:20 AM that night, the kerosene lamp placed on the table in front of the bed somehow fell over, causing the fire to spread to the mosquito net. The fire quickly became uncontrollable. Neighbors discovered the fire and reported it to the police, and the fire brigade immediately drove a pumper to put out the fire, which was eventually extinguished. Fortunately, the fire did not break through the roof, only burning the bed, curtains, and miscellaneous items in the room. However, the girl, Jin Di, who was sleeping in bed, was not rescued in time and perished in the fire. When the fire brigade pulled out the body, it was charred,

her forehead and skull were gone, her abdomen was broken, and her intestines were exposed, a horrific sight. When the fire alarm sounded, Chen Du returned from her stroll. When she arrived at the entrance of the lane, she heard the alarm and mistakenly thought it was a robbery, so she did not dare to enter the lane. When the fire was extinguished and she entered the lane, she learned that there had been a fire at her home and that her daughter had already been burned to death. She ran to the door, wailing as she embraced the body.

Later, the police station sent detectives to carry the body to the Tongren Fuyuan branch for an autopsy. Yesterday, the Second Special District Court was notified, and Prosecutor Wang Ren went to the scene and confirmed that the deceased had been burned alive. After questioning the mother, he ordered the body to be released to the mother for burial.

Wang Jincai Died Tragically from His Injuries

The Body Will Be Sent to Shanghai for Examination

Wang Jincai, a villager from Dongmachang in Datuan Township, Pudong, was a Taoist priest, nearly sixty years old, with an elderly mother, children, and grandchildren,

Conviction for Harming a Young Girl 167

Zhang Yongsheng Sentenced to Seven Years of Imprisonment

Binghua Laoliu, formerly a prostitute, gave birth to a daughter while working as such. She later married an Englishman named Tana, who is currently a detective in the Public Concession police force. The girl was taken along and Tana treated her as his own, naming her Mengna Tana. She is now six years old. Recently, she was abused by Zhang Yongsheng and Zhu Asong, servants at their residence, causing injuries to her lower body. Binghua Laoliu then informed her husband Tana, who dismissed Zhang and reported the matter to the police, who arrested both men and brought them to the First Special District Local Court,

accusing them of raping a young girl. This was previously reported in this newspaper. It is now learned that Judge Liu has thoroughly investigated the case. Yesterday morning, the two defendants, Zhang and Zhu, were brought before the court, and the verdicts were announced. Zhang Yongsheng was sentenced to seven years of imprisonment for raping a girl under the age of sixteen. Zhu Asong was sentenced to three years of imprisonment for indecent behavior towards a girl under the age of sixteen. The number of days spent in custody will be deducted from their sentences at a rate of one day for every two days served.

After the verdicts were announced, the police took the two criminals back into custody to await confirmation before being sent to prison to serve their sentences.

China Economic Credit

Overview of the Cooperative Society Over the Past Year 168

In recent years, the social economy has gradually declined, and the economy of the general public has been particularly panicked. Mr. Zhang Shouyong and Mr. Qiu Hanping of this city, in order to promote cooperation and seek an economic way out for the common people, founded the China Economic Credit Cooperative Society last winter. To this day, it has been a year, and the achievements are quite remarkable. The general situation is as follows: (1) Organizational system: The highest authority of the society is the general meeting of shareholders, which elects the board of directors and the board of supervisors. The board of

directors appoints the general manager. Under the general manager, there are four departments: documentation, administration, accounting, and

cashier, and four divisions: savings, loans, mutual assistance, and investigation. There are also an investment review committee and an investment fund management committee. Zhang Shouyong is the chairman of the board, Qiu Hanping is the general manager, and the standing directors are Qiu Hanping, Zhang Yongnian, Xia Fengqi, Zhuang Zutong, and Chen Kan (Xia, Zhuang, and Chen also serve as directors of the savings, accounting, and documentation departments). Liu Daofang is the director of the mutual assistance division, Zheng Tianren is the director of the administrative department, and Lin Kanghou, Xie Xiaochu, Zhang Yuelian, Xi Yushu, Pan Gongzhan, Wu Xingya, and others are members of the fund management committee. There are about ten other staff members, all of whom have a deep understanding of their work. Among them, Zhang Shouyong and Qiu Hanping are the most responsible and hardworking. (2) Business situation: Cooperative movement is still in its infancy in China, and most people are indifferent to cooperative undertakings. Therefore, it is often not easy for general cooperative societies to develop. However, the society's methods are excellent and have won social sympathy. In the past year, the number of members has increased to more than a thousand, and the amount of social funds recognized each month varies, with some saving five yuan per month, and some saving ten or fifteen yuan per month. The society's savings are all managed by the management committee, which uses them properly and invests prudently.

A portion is also used for loans to members, which is convenient for them. It is estimated that at least several thousand yuan are loaned out each month. (3) Mutual assistance undertakings:

The society is very enthusiastic in handling mutual assistance affairs for its members. The most notable achievements are legal advice, medical advice, guidance for further education, free schooling, preferential shopping in stores, and lodging in hostels. (4) Entertainment facilities: The society has an entertainment room, a reading room, a conference room, and a billiard room, with a radio, various chess and ball games, and various books and newspapers. (5) The society has made great efforts to promote cooperation. Special supplements have been attached to major newspapers in this city for the opening ceremony and the solicitation of members. The Economic Cooperation Monthly, the Economic Cooperation Weekly, and the Society News have been published successively. The Economic Cooperation Weekly is distributed as a supplement to the Morning Post, and the Society News is edited and printed by the society itself and is still being published. (5) Society facilities: The society's offices are located in a three-story

Western-style building at the intersection of Hankou Road and Shilu Road, Tong'an Lane. The ground floor is the general office and dining room, the second floor is the entertainment room, reading room, conference room, billiard room, and manager's office, and the third floor is the hostel, dormitory, and bathroom. It is said that due to the development of the business, the current address is not sufficient for office use, and it will soon be moved to No. 918, Edward Road, which is opposite the Nanjing Grand Theater, and is larger in scale and

convenient for transportation.

Social Affairs Bureau

Band Registration Deadline Approaching 169

Those Not Registered Will Not Be Allowed to Operate

The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau is organizing the registration of Western bands and sheet music in the city in order to rectify the bands in this city. It is learned that more than a hundred bands have applied for registration, and most of them have received their registration certificates.

The registration period will end at the end of October. From November onwards, when applying to the Public Security Bureau for a permit for ceremonial processions for weddings and funerals, the registration certificate of the hired band must be presented for verification. Therefore, bands that have not registered after the deadline will not be allowed to operate. All unregistered bands should apply within the deadline for their own benefit. The registration procedures are very simple. Application forms can be obtained from the Social Affairs Bureau and submitted without any charge.

Over a Hundred People Petitioned the Municipal Government Yesterday 173

The Municipal Government Agreed to Investigate and Handle

The residents of a section of Wuzhen Road, Zhabei North (between Xinmin Road and Xinjiang Road), all live in houses built with lead sheets, totaling about a hundred households. Because the landlord, Yuchang Company, through the rent collector Ji Kunlin, erected bamboo fences around the houses and ordered all the residents to move out completely within three days,

they were in a state of panic. Yesterday morning at 9:00 AM, they gathered more than a hundred residents, set out in a group, and went to the Municipal Government to petition. They elected Zhang Rongji, Xue Jinbiao, Jiang Zhiyou, Lu Chunjiang, and Zhang Jiabao as the five general representatives. When they arrived at the Municipal Government, the five representatives, including Zhang Rongji, entered, while the remaining residents waited outside the gate. The Municipal Government sent someone to meet them, asked about their intentions, accepted the petition brought by the representatives, and promised to investigate and handle it. The representatives then withdrew and led all the residents back.

Special Item

Awakening to National Self-Reliance and Revival 184

By Zhang Ruoji

| At the China Vocational Education Society |

Introduction | Today, I am honored to be invited by the China Vocational Education Society to speak here, to gather with all of you and study together. It is a great pleasure. The rain is very heavy today, it hasn't stopped all day, and all of you have braved the rain to come here. This spirit is especially admirable to me.

The topic for today is divided into nine sections, but based on my previous experience of speaking at the Youth Association and various universities,

each time it always takes two or three hours. This topic is even more complex, and I'm afraid the time allotted today won't be enough to fully explore it. I hope that everyone will continue to study on their own.

1. The Origin of the Topic: The reason I want to talk about this topic today is based on my consistent central idea. I dare not consider myself extraordinary, imitating Confucius by saying, "My Way is consistent." But I firmly believe that I do have a consistent idea. This consistent idea is nationalism. Every day, or rather, every moment, whether studying, writing, working, or returning home, I never forget our nation. I can say that I am a thorough and ardent believer in nationalism. Therefore, no matter what I speak about, what kind of knowledge I study, or what kind of problem I consider, my starting and ending points are always based on the nation. This is the initial reason why I want to talk about this topic. The method of learning should naturally be based on a scientific spirit and a calm, objective attitude. I myself study politics, especially public law.

However, when I study specialized knowledge, I always bring some emotion into it. Originally, a specialized scholar should have a scientific and rational mind, and should not mix in personal feelings. Emotional impulses are something that scholars should not have. But why do I deliberately violate this? There are many reasons, which cannot be explained in a single sentence. Simply put,

I advocate that emotion and reason should be developed in a balanced way. Therefore, no matter what kind of issue I discuss, I always carry strong and fervent emotions.

For example, when I study the constitution, I also bring the spirit and emotion of nationalism. Last year, I wrote an essay on the nation and the constitution in the Ta Kung Pao. My theory is probably not found in the constitutional law of any country in the world. This is also because it is influenced by my consistent ideas. Some people may laugh at me for studying in this way, saying, "You want to nationalize everything. What will your knowledge become?" In fact, the reason why we seek knowledge, and what we value about having knowledge, is simply to contribute it to our nation, to maintain and advance the long and great life of the nation. Without the interests of the nation, there is no value in knowledge. Without the foundation of national survival, we cannot create a system of knowledge. Therefore, I firmly believe in myself. Whether I am studying, working, speaking anywhere, or writing articles in my room, I should not deviate from this so-called foundation of national life. This is what all of us who study knowledge should encourage ourselves with. Today, while I explain the origin of the topic, I also sincerely advise everyone to enrich their knowledge and abilities based on this spirit, to promote the culture of our Chinese nation, and to save the nation from its current plight. Especially during this period of severe national crisis, the mission that we intellectuals bear should be especially significant.

2. National Revival and the Relationship of "Power": A few days ago, a friend came from Beiping. He is a chief editor in a major newspaper in Beiping, and he is also a renowned professor at the six universities in Beiping. He was also a good classmate of mine in Europe. When talking to him about the issue of national revival, he said, "I feel that national revival is an issue of 'power.' Politics is also 'power.' How can we use this 'power' to promote politics and revive the nation? This is a major issue that we should pay attention to at present." I then followed up by asking him, "Then where is this 'power'?" This is the starting point for my creation of the "self-reliance" doctrine. Since the national crisis, domestic public opinion and popular sentiment have been very激昂, very慷慨, and very fervent. Among these many激昂慷慨 opinions and popular sentiments, we can certainly find many valuable opinions and theories that are worthy of our admiration. However, we cannot deny that some of them are empty and superficial. I think this is because the general public has been subjected to intuitive impulses without adding calm and rational consideration. I believe that reason and emotion should be balanced. Therefore, what we see and hear everywhere are theories and articles that are purely intuitive impulses. These kinds of theories and articles cannot actually save the nation. For example, generally people only advocate resisting Japan and saving the country in words, but in reality, they are not prepared at all. No one can say "no" to this kind of theory on the surface, but we must ask, where is the "power" to resist Japan? Is our national defense consolidated? Whether in terms of the people, the government, or various aspects, do we have the real strength to resist Japan? Despite慷慨激昂 speaking about resisting Japan, despite never forgetting to resist Japan psychologically, do we actually have the power to resist Japan? Do we have the means to resist Japan? They don't ask, don't research, and don't prepare. They are simply indulging in emotions, singing irresponsible high-sounding tunes that please people temporarily. Even more painful is that the purpose of a few people is only to激昂on the surface, to please the public, to seize the opportunity, and to show off their personal style.

There are too many opportunists in China today. There is speculation in being an official, and there is also speculation in doing patriotic movements. Seizing the opportunity of the national crisis, they say a few irresponsible words that please people temporarily, so that everyone will support them, and they use this power to gain a position and develop their own future and selfish desires. This kind of inconsistency between words and actions, opportunistic elements who deceive the public, cannot save the country. They can even be said to be criminals of the country. I remember that after the September 18th Incident, we had a meeting to discuss the issue of resisting Japan. I proposed twelve plans for resisting Japan, but they did not understand my proposal at all. I went back home in great sorrow and wrote an article with tears (titled "Vow to Save the Nation"), which was published in the Central Daily News and the China Times. This article

told the truth, without a single embellishment. Later, many newspapers and many places reprinted my article. Some friends even said that the value of my article was almost the same as Fichte's "Addresses to the German Nation." It can be seen that although my theory cannot be adopted immediately, it will eventually not be permanently buried. Therefore, since the national crisis, I have been determined to sing a "low-key tune." I am still singing a low-key tune now. Regardless of whether anyone agrees with me, I will not use this to steal a false reputation for myself, find a way out, or seek a position. It is not because others are singing high-key tunes that I especially want to sing a low-key tune to be different. I feel that the current decline of the Chinese nation, and the origin of the current severe national crisis, are definitely not the result of a single day. I can say that the decline of our nation and the current national crisis are caused by the "inertia" of the people's society over thousands of years. Our nation is dominated by deeply rooted social "inertia," and all social activities and the power of the people cannot be developed. Therefore, no matter which aspect of the country,

whether it is literary, military, economic, political, social,

or educational, all kinds of undertakings have not made significant progress.

Although China is a culturally advanced country, Chinese culture has been suppressed by this kind of "great inertia" for thousands of years and has not been able to develop.

Therefore, as the most advanced cultural country, it has now become the most落后 and without a country, or the country with the slowest cultural progress. Because of this reason, everything that follows culture, such as politics, economics, and military affairs, cannot be generated, and it becomes a nation without "power." Since the nation has no "power," it is naturally unavoidable to fail in the law of survival of the fittest. According to the principle of sociology, the direction of human development is originally towards the direction of the least resistance. Japan, seeing that China has no "power,"

it developed its militarism, its imperialism, and all its aggression from this direction. Therefore, the reason for the decline of our nation and the formation of the national crisis did not start with the September 18th Incident. The roots of the disaster have long been buried.

If we want to save the country today, the first thing we must do is to understand the reason for the decline of the nation, study how to enrich national power, and prepare to enrich national power in a down-to-earth and exemplary manner. Now that we know the reason for the decline of the nation, on the one hand, we must eliminate the "inertia" that hinders national development, and on the other hand, we must actively prepare for the development of "national power." With sound national power, there will naturally be the power to resist Japan and the power to revive the nation.

Reading Q&A 187

Notice of Suspension of Publication of "Reading Q&A"

Time passes very quickly. "Reading Q&A" has met with you for a full nine months. Except for the Lunar New Year and the occasional suspension of publication for no more than ten times due to insufficient space in this newspaper,

tens of thousands of readers have been reading it every day. We are very honored that we have gained so many sympathizers in spirit, but on the other hand, we cannot help but feel ashamed.

What have we given to the readers after all? On this eve of suspension of publication, we have reflected on it earnestly. Before parting, we cannot help but make a self-confession. We cannot help but admit that what we have given to others, if not zero, is too limited.

This is by no means a humble statement. First, because "Reading Q&A" is only a part of the work of this department, and this department itself is only a department of the library, we do not have more sufficient time to make "Reading Q&A" more vibrant and more practical. Second, because of the space limitations of this newspaper, news articles are often crowded, and for a poor "Reading Q&A" article, it often has to be cut into several paragraphs, so that readers are not connected before and after,

and reading it is the same as not reading it. Third, because the people who write Reading Q&A,

are mostly a few bookworms, too far removed from the actual lives of shop assistants and apprentices, and what they write inevitably still carries the atmosphere of scholars, and cannot make people who really have no education approach it. Fourth, we are also subject to many well-intentioned criticisms and strict corrections from various aspects. We勉强尽棉力 and want to be detached, but we are really exhausted and cannot live up to everyone's expectations. In short, looking back on ourselves, besides shame, there is only self-blame. Now we don't want to continue doing this work that we can't do. We respectfully thank and apologize to everyone who cares about us.

What about in the future? We are library workers, and our work of reading guidance in the library will not stop because of this. On the contrary, we will concentrate our efforts on other aspects. At the same time, we can add a note to comfort readers that the Reading Life Society will soon publish a reading magazine called Reading Life Bi-monthly. In the future, any questions about reading, or that publication may also talk about it. Now that we have temporarily canceled this corner of the newspaper, we probably won't feel too lonely.

Before and after, we sincerely hope that readers will always take new knowledge in life. Today's China must be in a very rich era. As long as you are loyal to life and diligent in taking,

there is really nowhere that you cannot gain knowledge. We advise you to study hard, but at the same time, don't believe in books too much. We advise you to spend one minute reading in the streets and markets, and don't go back to the book room with bright windows and clean desks. And wish you all take care.

Special announcement from the Reading Guidance Department ·· Although the Reading Q&A edited by this department has been announced to be suspended, we have not stopped guiding the readers of this library or this newspaper in reading because of this. If readers have any doubts about books, they can still ask them as much as possible and discuss them with us.

We will do our best to answer them in individual replies. In the future, readers' letters should still be sent to the Reading Guidance Department, Circulation Library, Shen Bao, 3rd Floor, Continental Shopping Center, Nanjing Road, Shanghai.

Special Issue of the Children's Library

Talking about Children's Library from the Standpoint of Education 188

— Dong Renjian

People, especially when they are young children, as long as parents or society have the ability to bear it, there is no one who does not want to give him a good education.

But why should one receive education, what kind of education should one receive, and is there a relatively simple way to receive a good education.

We don't need to talk about profound academic theories. Simply put, education is nothing more than to be a person, that is, to let young children know people's things and affairs, understand people's words and thoughts, and perceive people's joys, anger, sorrows, and happiness, so that he can get along with people and cooperate with people, and then he can join people's society, and people will not abandon him outside society. In other words: The root of education lies in making young children "humanized".

Of course, young children from birth, are immersed in people's experiences: what he sees are nothing but people's things and affairs, what he hears are nothing but people's words and thoughts, what he feels are nothing but people's joys, anger, sorrows, and happiness. However, what he sees may not be very clear for a while, what he hears may not be very clear for a while, and what he feels may not be very touching for a while. He often looks like this, looks like that, and looks like something else; asks this, asks that, and asks something else: What is this? What is this used for? Where does this come from? Is this always like this? How is it done? Who did it? Can I do it··· Educators should answer these questions for him, and education is in these questions and answers! If we can answer him, answer him fully, and answer him interestingly, he will look again, ask again, and feel and observe again, from one point to another, from one step to another, until he can answer himself and progress himself.

We know that contemporary society is no longer as simple as it used to be. It is easy to see, hear, and feel. Even ordinary adults there can recognize and perceive social affairs and objects there even if they recognize and perceive, they there can know how to show it to young children, explain it so that young children can understand it, and stimulate it so that young children feel it even parents who are very close to young children, even kindergartens and low-grade elementary school teachers who have teaching experience also seem to be difficult to guarantee that they will be effective. Therefore, whether in the family or in the school, whether it is parents, teachers, or young children themselves, they all need a kind of excellent guidance, learning tools, and a medium for humanization. From the standpoint of education, the reporter believes that this is the real contribution of the "Children's Library" published by the Commercial Press. We have specially made the following "Chart of Children's Development and Children's Library" to express this meaning and wish this "Children's Library" success and the continued efforts of those who edit and publish this new library.

Dissection of the Children's Library 189

— Xu Yingchang

I remember that during Children's Day this year, I wrote an article entitled "From Children's Day to the Children's Books of the Commercial Press." The main content was about giving good children's books to children on Children's Day and giving a brief introduction to the various types of books contained in the Elementary School Students' Library. Finally, I mentioned that the books in the Elementary School Students' Library were suitable for the upper grades of elementary school, and I hoped that the Commercial Press would publish a complete set of readings for the lower grades of elementary school in the near future.

Indeed, lower elementary school students also want to enjoy interesting readings and have a desire for knowledge. If we are prejudiced against lower elementary school students and do not provide them with books of a comparable level, we would not only be unfair to general lower elementary school students but also go against the principles of education. This matter should not be ignored. Moreover, the "Teaching Points for Elementary School Chinese Language Curriculum" formulated by the Ministry of Education also mentioned, "In addition to intensive reading each week, there should be regular guidance for extensive reading" and "Besides in-class guidance, children should be urged to read extensively outside of class..." In order to fulfill the mission of providing extracurricular reading materials for lower elementary school students, the Commercial Press actively carried out the editing and printing of this Children's Library after the completion of the Elementary School Students' Library to meet the needs of lower elementary school students.

The Children's Library went through careful planning and was successfully completed with the cooperation of more than thirty colleagues with rich teaching and writing experience. It will soon be able to meet with children all over the country. In order to make people all over the country understand the content of the Children's Library, we specially dissected its content, hoping for corrections from domestic children's education experts, elementary school teachers, and parents.

(1) The Selection of Materials for This Library

Whether editing and printing a single book or a series of children's books, if the selection of materials is solely aimed at catering to children's low-level interests, such books are not only useless but also harmful to children. The selection of materials for this library has been repeatedly deliberated and detailed editing regulations have been formulated. The content of each book is entirely centered on the revitalization of the nation, such as promoting labor production, instructing on resisting foreign aggression and saving the country, cultivating civic morality, and enlightening scientific knowledge. All of these aspects have been taken into consideration. Materials containing selfishness, profiteering, contention, passivity, timidity, pessimism, restraint, and feudal ideas are all avoided. In addition, attention is paid to materials about children's activities: there are things to sing, things to play, and things to do. All activities that children love are collected as much as possible. The entire book consists mostly of original material.

(2) The Level of This Library

This library is edited according to the level of lower elementary school students, with books as the mainstay, supplemented by short textual explanations. Elementary school students who have read half or one volume of Chinese textbooks can read on their own with only slight guidance from teachers or parents.

(3) The Categories of This Library

This library refers to the subjects in the curriculum standards for lower elementary schools and divides the content into twelve categories: society, civics, nature, arithmetic, hygiene, physical education, labor, art, poetry, language, riddles, and stories. Everything that lower elementary school students should have is included. Now, we analyze the proportion of each category of materials in the first collection of 200 books in this library as follows:

Category Number of Books % Category Number of Books %

Society 29 14.5 Civics 16 8.0

Nature 41 20.5 Arithmetic 4 2.0

Hygiene 11 5.5 Physical Education 3 1.5

Labor 8 4.0 Art 5 2.5

Poetry 7 3.5 Language 4 2.0

Riddles 4 2.0 Stories 78 39.0

Total 200 100.0

If we summarize the twelve categories of materials, they can be divided into two major categories: (A) those related to knowledge and skills, such as society, civics, nature, arithmetic, hygiene, physical education, labor, language, and riddles; (B) those related to appreciation, such as arithmetic, poetry, and stories.

Let's statistically analyze these two major categories of materials. Those belonging to knowledge and skills total 110 books, and those belonging to appreciation total 90 books. Comparing the two, the difference is negligible. Based on this ratio, we can know that the content of this library is balanced in both quality and quantity, without the drawback of favoring any one type of material.

(4) The Distribution of This Library

Due to the limitation of the number of books in the first collection of this library (200 books), each category cannot, of course, completely include all the necessary materials. However, after careful planning, we have accommodated the most important materials in each category as much as possible. Now, we will take the books included in the society category of this library as an example to briefly illustrate our plan for distributing each category.

There are 29 books in the society category of this library. The titles are as follows:

1. Lovable China 2. Shapes of Maps of Various Provinces

3. My Home 4. My Hometown

5. Our School 6. Our Library

7. Life of Ancient People 8. Tree Dwellers

9. Cave Dwellers 10. Clothing

11. Food 12. Shelter

12. Transportation 14. Street Sweeping

13. Firefighting 16. National Goods Exhibition

14. Hot Places 18. Cold Places

15. National Flags of Various Countries 20. Children of Various Countries

16. Sun Yat-sen 22. Yellow Flower Hill

17. Double Tenth Festival 24. Children's Day

18. Several Great People (Part 1) 26. Several Great People (Part 2)

19. Our Navy 28. Our Army

20. Our Air Force

The purpose of the above books, such as "Lovable China" and "Shapes of Maps of Various Provinces," is to arouse children's national consciousness. "My Home" and "My Hometown" can allow children to understand their own hometown. "Our School" and "Our Library" can enable children to understand the organization and environment of the school. "Life of Ancient People," "Tree Dwellers," "Clothing," "Food," "Shelter," and "Transportation" can enable children to understand the evolution of human life. Street sweeping and firefighting are materials related to social undertakings. The purpose of the National Goods Exhibition is to cultivate children's habit of using domestic goods. "Hot Places" and "Cold Places" are knowledge related to geography. "National Flags of Various Countries" and "Children of Various Countries" are materials related to international affairs. "Sun Yat-sen," Yellow Flower Hill, and the Double Tenth Festival aim to make children understand the contributions of the Premier and other martyrs to the founding of the Republic of China and to know the loveliness of National Day. Children's Day is closely related to children and can enable children to know to respect their own position. The representative figures in "Several Great People" are related to culture, some are patriotic heroes, some are scientists, and some are explorers, all of which can serve as models for children. "Our Navy," "Our Army," and "Our Air Force" can enable children to have some understanding of national defense equipment.

Looking at the content of the above books as a whole, we can get a glimpse of the appropriateness of the distribution of materials in this library and the closeness of the connections. The distribution of materials in other categories such as civics, nature, and arithmetic also has its own characteristics. Due to space limitations, it is not possible to list them all.

(5) The Style of This Library

Except for labor, art, poetry, and riddles, which are special in nature, each book in other categories in this library forms its own unit. The style of each book varies depending on the nature of the material. There are rhymed texts and prose. Rhymed texts are not limited to the poetry category; society, civics, nature, hygiene, physical education, riddles, etc., are also written in rhymed texts. Because rhymed texts have syllables, they can be recited, are easy to remember, and have a relatively strong interest in reading. Therefore, the materials in this library that can be compiled in rhymed texts are compiled in rhymed texts to increase children's reading efficiency.

(6) The Words and Sentences in This Library

The words used in each book of this library are extremely careful. First, they are based on the research results of various experts as a blueprint for the words used, and then a vocabulary of commonly used words is formulated with reference to the current textbooks for the lower grades of each subject. Then, the words used in each book of this library are determined based on the vocabulary. Regarding the organization of sentences, we strive to be concise. Each page has a maximum of no more than eight sentences, and each sentence has a maximum of no more than nine characters (some books, such as "My Toys" and "Zoo," require detailed explanations, so the sentences have to be slightly longer than the original standard, but this number does not exceed seven percent). The wording is completely suited to children's tone, so that young children can read easily and efficiency is increased.

Because this library has to comply with the curriculum standards, starting from the third grade of elementary school, there is a provision for "familiarity with the National Phonetic Alphabet," so the books in this library do not uniformly add phonetic symbols in order to be dedicated to use by lower-grade students.

The font of children's reading materials should be large, so that they can be clearly seen at a glance when reading, and it will not hurt eyesight. The font of this library is all regular script, the largest is equivalent to ordinary first-size lead characters, and the second largest is equivalent to ordinary second-size lead characters. The font is elegant and the strokes are clear, which can be used as a model for children's writing.

(7) The Illustrations in This Library

Children like to appreciate illustrations more enthusiastically than they appreciate text. Each book in this library has beautiful and lively illustrations, which on the one hand can give children a deep impression of the content of the book, and on the other hand can arouse children's interest in beauty, so that considerable educational benefits can be achieved in the illustrations.

Among the 200 books in the first collection of this library, 50 books are printed in five colors, 50 books are printed in two colors, and 100 books are printed in single-color ink. All things that need to express their authenticity are printed in five colors to give children an accurate understanding of certain things. For example, the books "Zoo," "Birds," "Butterflies and Moths," and "Our Fruits" are all examples of books printed in full color.

(8) The Paper in This Library

The paper for children's reading materials must be thicker than ordinary paper so that it is not easily damaged. The paper used in this library is 140-pound thick Swiss paper, which is strong and durable, so that each book can be preserved for a long time. The paper is not only white but also does not reflect light, which does not hurt eyesight. This is also a feature of this library.

(9) The Format of This Library

The format of children's reading materials should not be too large or too small. If the format is too large, it will not only take up a lot of space when stored, but it will also be inconvenient to carry. If the format is too small, the font and illustrations will have to be reduced, which will hinder children's learning psychology. The format of this library is 7.5 inches in height and 4 inches in width, the same size as the textbooks and children's books and newspapers published by this library, which is very convenient for storage and carrying.

(10) The Application of This Library

Because this library is rich in content, well-organized, has many illustrations, and the text is easy to understand, its scope of application is relatively wide. In addition to being specially provided for families to organize libraries, for children to read at home, and for school libraries to set up separate lower-grade reading rooms for lower-grade students to read at school, it can also be provided for adult libraries to set up separate children's reading sections for nearby children to read at the library; it can also be used as supplementary books for older illiterate people in various local mass education halls, farmer education halls, and public reading rooms.

The content and form of this library have been briefly dissected as above. As for the effects of the application of this library in various aspects after its publication, I will report on it when there is an opportunity.

Introduction to the Children's Library 190

— Fan Zhizhan

I remember that on last year's National Day, I published an article introducing the Elementary School Students' Library. It has been a full year since then. In the past year, it is said that more than 10,000 copies of the Elementary School Students' Library have been ordered across the country. According to a rough estimate, there should be about one million elementary school students reading it. The benefits gained by elementary school students from reading it must be great.

The content of the Elementary School Students' Library is suitable for upper elementary school students. If lower elementary school students are to be provided with reading materials, another library that is more simple and easy to understand must be compiled. In order to meet this need, the Commercial Press engaged in the editing of the Children's Library after the completion of the Elementary School Students' Library. Now the manuscripts have been collected and sent to print and are scheduled to be published. I think this work is very valuable, and its value can be said to be the same as that of the Elementary School Students' Library.

Compiling and printing a library that is truly suitable for children to read is indeed not an easy task. I think that at least the following points must be taken into account when compiling and printing such a library.

First, the entire library must have an overall plan and organization. Within the possible range, each book must also become a complete unit.

Second, all materials must be suitable for children's lives. Children can gradually develop their experience by reading them.

Third, the vocabulary used in each book must be easy for children to recognize and understand, and the sentence structure must also be suitable for children's tone.

Fourth, children like to appreciate illustrations very much. All illustrations must be vivid, lively, and full of interest.

Fifth, printing and binding must not only be beautiful but also strong and durable. Because beauty can easily arouse children's interest in reading, and strong binding can preserve it for a long time.

When we introduce the Children's Library, we cannot ignore the above five points, of course.

The first collection of the Children's Library has a total of 200 books, divided into twelve categories such as society, civics, nature, arithmetic, hygiene, physical education, labor, art, poetry, language, riddles, and stories, which include the knowledge, skills, and various activities that children should have. According to the editors, each category of materials has considerable connections, and each book is also as much as possible a self-contained unit. After reading, children will not only enrich their lives but also develop the ability to cope with the current society. The vocabulary used in the entire library is all based on evidence, and the sentence structure also takes children's tone into account as much as possible. All the illustrations have very lively lines and even more beautiful colors. The paper used is strong and thick and does not reflect light, so children can read without hurting their eyes.

Therefore, in fact, the Children's Library can take care of the above five points. In our country, where children's reading materials are scarce, the great effect of providing this Children's Library for children across the country to read is not difficult to imagine.

If elementary schools across the country lack supplementary reading materials for lower grades, if families are willing to seek educational happiness for their children, and if libraries want to establish children's sections, I think this Children's Library will definitely provide great help.

Ministry of Education Explains Joint Entrance Examination

Supplementary Examination Method for One Failing Subject 207

The Ministry of Education, in response to the inquiry from the Nanjing Municipal Social Affairs Bureau regarding the supplementary examination method for students who fail one or two subjects in the joint entrance examination, specifically instructed the bureau, stating that students who fail one or two subjects in the graduation joint entrance examination may participate in the next joint entrance examination for a maximum of two times. If they are unable to participate in the first or second time due to reasons or illness and have concrete proof, they may be allowed to participate in the third or fourth joint entrance examination, etc.

General Situation of the National Compilation and Translation Bureau 208

The National Compilation and Translation Bureau was established in June of the 21st year of the Republic of China. The bureau is located on Shanxi Road in Nanjing. Its organization is as follows: Under the director, there are three groups: humanities, nature, and affairs. Currently, there are three directors, six specialized translators, eight contracted translators, eleven translators, five clerks, five office workers, and twenty-two clerks. The total number of personnel in the bureau is seventy-one. Its expenses were only more than 7,000 yuan per month when it was established. By July of the 22nd year, the central government approved 12,000 yuan per month. Its work is divided into two main parts: compiling and translating terms for various subjects, monographs, textbooks, and other materials; and reviewing textbooks for primary and secondary schools.

In the part of compiling and translating terms, the following five books have been announced and published by the Ministry of Education: "Astronomical Terms," "Physics Terms," "Chemical Naming Principles," "Mineralogical Terms," and "Music Terms." The following books are being compiled and will be announced soon:

"Academic Terms," "Electrical Terms," "Chemical Instrument Terms," "Chemical Terminology and Terminology," "Geological Terms," "Petrological Terms," "Animal Embryology

Terms," "Comparative Anatomy Terms," "Bacteriology and Immunology Terms," "Psychopathology Terms," "Parasitology Terms," "Pathology Terms," "Psychology Terms," and thirteen other books.

In the part of compiling and translating monographs, the following have been published: "The Improvement of Chinese Education,"

"American Government and Politics, Volume 1," "History of the Chinese Nation's Colonization of Nanyang,"

"Basic Principles of Economics," "Meteorology," "Chinese Financial Problems, Volume 1," "Principles of Gestalt Psychology," "Five Major Dialogues of Plato by Four Contemporary British Novelists," "On the Works of Kepler's Astronomy," "Research on Optics," "Experiments on Smoking Agents and Explosions," "Experimental Methods for Preparing Explosives,"

"Experimental Methods for Preparing Gaseous Gases," "Plant Geography," "Textbooks and Remarks on Anti-Chinese Xenophobia," and "Modern Psychological Schools," eighteen books in total. The following are in printing: "Chronicle of Major Educational Events in China in the Past Seventy Years," "Wartime Economics," "On Wartime Controlled Economy," "Public Finance," "China's Cotton Textile Industry,"

"Human Learning," "Theory of Celestial Bodies," "Pia Qiao Differential Equations," "Introduction to the Precision and Graphical Method of Diagrams," "General Theory of Chemical Warfare," "Chemical Principles," "Chemical Literature," "Zoology," and thirteen books in total. The following are under review and will be ready for printing: "Modern European Political and Social History," "Anthropological Studies of Southwestern China," "Chronicle of Major Events in China in the Past Three Hundred Years," "History of the Development of British Novels," "Thoughts of a Soldier," "Elementary Calculus," "Theoretical Mechanics," "Experimental Methods for Organic Chemistry," "Organic Chemistry," "Plant Physiology," "Catalog of Chinese Herbal Medicine Specimens," and eleven books in total. The following are being compiled: "Wireless Electricity," "Differential Geometry," "History of British Literature," "Brief History of Modern Psychology," "China's Salt Administration Policy," "The Gate of Schilla," "Yellow River Chronicle," "American Government and Politics, Volume 2," "Italian Government and Politics," "Chinese Financial Problems, Volume 2," and ten books in total.

In the part of compiling textbooks, there are textbooks for short-term primary schools, the "Three Principles of the People Thousand-Character Textbook," "Chinese-Mongolian Joint

Primary School Chinese Textbook," "Special Chinese Readers for Primary Schools," "Social Textbooks for Primary Schools," "Natural Textbooks for Primary Schools," "Special Chinese Readers for Secondary Schools," "Course of Intensive Reading in Chinese for Junior High Schools," "Chinese Textbooks for Senior High Schools," and eight books in total. In addition, there are also "Book Reviews," fourteen issues, "Chemical Special Issue," "Astronomical, Mathematical, and Physical Special Issue," "Catalog of Children's Readings," "Catalog of Reference Books for Middle School Students," "Index of the Donghua Records," "Comparative Table of Modern Chinese and Western History," and seven other types.

In the part of reviewing textbooks for primary and secondary schools, more than 400 types and more than 2,000 copies have been submitted for review. More than 50 types of primary school textbooks and more than 50 types of secondary school textbooks have been approved for review. 20 types of books for primary schools and 40 types of books for secondary schools have been approved for publication. 6 types of books for primary schools and more than 40 types of books for secondary schools have not been approved for review. The bureau has been established for only two years, and it has worked hard on academic work with only a small amount of funding, and the results are quite impressive.

Zhejiang Organizes Education Properties in Various Counties 209

The Department of Education Formulates Regulations and Submits Articles

The education properties of various counties in Zhejiang Province have not been cleared up for a long time. Now, the Department of Education has formulated the "Regulations of the Committee for Organizing Education Properties in Various Counties of Zhejiang Province" and submitted it to the Provincial Government Conference for resolution and approval, so as to organize and establish it within the shortest possible time and be responsible for organizing it. The regulations are recorded as follows: Article 1: The Department of Education shall establish a Committee for Organizing Education Properties in Various Counties in order to organize the education properties of various counties. Article 2: The members of this committee shall be organized by the secretary of the Department of Education, the director of the responsible section, section members, and all supervisors. Article 3: This committee shall have three standing committee members, who shall be appointed by the director of the Department of Education from among the committee members.

Preside over daily affairs and take turns as chairman during meetings. Article 4: This committee shall be divided into two groups, investigation and clearance, with one director for each group, who shall be appointed by the director of the Department of Education from among the committee members. The duties of each group are as follows: (1) Investigation Group: Investigates the situation of properties in various counties. (2) Clearance Group: Dispatches personnel to various counties to implement clearance. Article 5: This committee shall have one to two administrative staff members,

who shall be appointed concurrently by the director of the Department of Education from among the administrative staff members or clerks in the department. Article 6: When clearing the education properties of various counties, if it is considered that it cannot be handled by the personnel of this committee, special personnel may be hired to assist in the handling. The salary and travel expenses of the special personnel shall be paid from the office expenses of the Department of Education.

Article 7: The procedures for the organizing committee to clear the education properties of various counties shall be formulated separately. Article 8: The meetings of this committee shall have no fixed schedule and shall be convened by the standing committee members at any time. Article 9: This committee shall be attached to the Department of Education. Article 10: These regulations shall be implemented on the date of publication.

Zhejiang Aquatic Products School Experiences Student Uprising 210

The Zhejiang Dinghai Provincial Aquatic Products School, since the resignation of President Jin Kuangzhong,

has been appointed by the Department of Construction to be taken over by Wu Zhongyuan this semester. Unexpectedly, as soon as Wu took office, he was dissatisfied by the students of the school, and recently a student uprising occurred, resolutely retaining former President Jin. On the morning of the 4th of this month, the school gate posted a white cloth banner saying "Farewell to Wu Zhongyuan." The faculty and staff of the school held a meeting and agreed to take action with the students. At 2:00 PM that afternoon, President Wu Zhongyuan and Director Fu were forced to leave the school and escorted to the pier by the Public Security Bureau. After Wu and others entered the boat, they closed the doors and windows tightly for fear of students entering. Currently, the school administration is maintained by the faculty and staff. The students requested that classes continue as usual, but firmly stated that they did not want Wu to come back to resume his post.

It is reported that Wu has reported the details of the incident to the Department in Hangzhou after transferring from Shanghai.
