China Educational Film Association

Shanghai Branch Holds Board Meeting 215

Discussing the matter of collecting educational film fees

and assisting in the progress of the educational film troupe

The Shanghai Branch of the China Educational Film Association held its sixth board meeting the other day. Those present were Zhang Xingbai, Pan Gongzhan, Chen Baichen, Kuang Zhengqiu, Li Zhaobao, Kuang Minshi, Zhou Jianyun, Lu Shibai, Xu Gongmei, Chen Songchun, etc.

The matters discussed were: 1. Whether or not to add members to the fund custody committee of this branch. It was resolved to add one principal each from private primary and secondary schools to serve as members of the fund custody committee of this branch. 2. Correspondence from Municipal Chongzheng and other schools requesting that poor children be exempted from educational film fees and how to handle this. It was resolved that the number of students exempted from educational film fees should be based on the number of students approved for exemption by the Municipal Education Bureau. 3. Correspondence from Municipal Chongzheng and other schools requesting that educational film fees that have been received be paid off in one lump sum, and those that have not been received be paid in installments, and how to handle this. It was resolved that members of the association would be dispatched to collect the educational film fees from primary and secondary schools. If, because all fees have already been collected when school started, it is inconvenient to collect them separately, in order to avoid trouble for the schools, they may be instructed to formally send a letter stating the number of people,

and the fees will be collected in supplementary installments when school starts next semester. 4. Municipal Chongzheng and other schools requested that the badges be exempt from payment and issued free of charge, and how to handle this. It was resolved that educational film viewing badges need not be produced again. The guarantee deposits for these badges have already been paid to the association by each school and will be returned (the schools should bring the association's general receipt to the meeting to collect them). 5. Regarding the collection of educational film fees, there are occasionally a few schools that refuse to pay, and how to handle this. It was resolved that the Education Bureau will dispatch personnel to assist members of this association in collecting fees from the schools. 6. A report stated that the International Alliance had sent a letter to the general association, requesting that schools at all levels in our country be consulted to organize educational film pioneer teams to make full use of films and increase educational efficiency. The Department of Education has instructed each provincial and municipal education bureau to investigate and handle this matter. This branch's responsibility lies in assisting in the progress of the case, and how to assist in the progress of the case. It was resolved that specific methods will be drafted and submitted for discussion at the next meeting.

The presidium consisted of Zhang Xibo, Sheng Zhensheng, and Sun Zhenchun. After the formalities were observed, the chairman, Sun Zhenchun, reported.

Representatives delivered speeches one after another, and then the election was held. However, due to lack of time,

the ballots have not yet been counted.

Pan Gongzhan Delivers a Patriotic Speech 217

The Patriotic Girls' Middle School held a memorial week at 11 a.m. the day before yesterday. Mr. Pan Gongzhan, the Director of the Municipal Education Bureau, was invited to give instructions. Mr. Pan arrived at the school,

and after being introduced by the principal, Ji Yisheng, he delivered a speech to the students entitled "A Patriotic Plan," the main points of which were: "The method of patriotism requires the preparation of three kinds of power: (1) self-reliance, (2) self-defense, and (3) organizational power. The emergence of self-reliance lies in the development of intelligence and ability, and its purpose is to seek self-production and not rely on others. The emergence of self-defense lies in the tempering of physical strength, and its purpose is to resist insults and defend against enemies to ensure survival.

The emergence of organizational power lies in the possession of morality, and its purpose is to gather individuals to form a nation, so that the ability of self-reliance and self-defense can achieve the greatest effect. In the past, people divided morality into public morality and private morality, which is a great mistake. Morality cannot be established without society. In other words, the cultivation of self-reliance is intellectual education, the cultivation of self-defense is physical education, and the cultivation of organizational power is moral education. The production of these three components all belongs to self-confidence. If young students can be confident that they have self-reliance, self-defense, and organizational power, then the desire for patriotism can be fulfilled." Mr. Pan was energetic, and his speech lasted for more than an hour without fatigue, repeatedly citing analogies, and his attitude was extremely sincere. The three or four hundred people in the audience were all solemnly moved, as if they had received timely rain and transformation.

Another shipment of foreign wheat is confirmed

Futures wheat consistently decline

Yesterday's flour market opened lower due to reports of lower prices from abroad by 3-4 jiao. Spot foreign wheat also followed suit. The factories immediately started selling off their stock, causing the price to open lower and then gradually decline. At noon, prices for all months fell by 1-2 fen. In the afternoon, another shipment of foreign wheat was confirmed, causing the price to fall another 5 fen compared to the previous day.

It was only 4.57 yuan, and foreign merchants were still lowering prices to sell, so the first session in the afternoon saw another sudden drop of 2-3 fen, 4-5 fen lower than the previous day's closing price. Fortunately, the northern merchants made small purchases, and the market stabilized again. The closing price for this month was down 2.75 fen, next month was down 4.25 fen, December was down 3.75 fen, January was down 4 fen, and February was down 3.75 fen.

Wheat: Yesterday's wheat market opened higher in the morning due to the rebound the previous day. Hoarders liquidated and new shorts sold, and foreign wheat prices were reported lower, causing flour prices to fall. Sentiment was weak, and the opening price was immediately 4-5 fen lower. In the afternoon, with the confirmation of a shipment of foreign wheat and the flour market declining further, selling pressure on the market increased, and the decline was even greater. As a result, October was down 8 fen, November was down 6 fen, and December and January were down 7 fen each. February was down 9 fen. 1,000 bags of spot wheat were opened and handled by Fuxin, Gaofeng, and Shenda. Gao Che wheat was 3.30 yuan, with medium and lower grades also declining.

Kiln Middle Baige Falls by 3 Jiao 233

Shanghai South: Yesterday, the sources of goods were slightly more plentiful, with over twenty numbers arriving, totaling over 3,000 shi. Sales were normal, and sentiment was even weaker. In addition, the National Day holiday was the day after tomorrow.

Sellers with more new goods were eager to sell, making the situation even weaker. Although there were purchases, such as the Qingdao merchants buying over 200 bags of kiln middle grade,

it did not reverse the trend. Furthermore, the local sales of Baige were sluggish, leading to price cuts to attract buyers, causing prices to plummet. The price of kiln middle Baige fell by 3 jiao. New white rice and other thick new japonica rice arrived in small quantities and softened accordingly. Only new Du Yangjian was in short supply, and the stores were eager to stock up, so it remained firm. Other varieties of broken rice and Yantai rice were handled late in the evening, close to 100 bags of late rice, but because the local market was stagnant, the overall market was flat and weak. The exchange rate also continued to be sluggish, and the price gradually depreciated. New exchange bills were in short supply and had no market. New white coins opened at 9.40 yuan.

Shanghai North: Yesterday, the first 21 or 22 boats arrived from the river merchants. All goods on the market

were selling well. New and old white japonica rice and new Yang Du tip and old white coin were trading well. Kiln rice was scarce. The remaining goods were flat. Broken japonica and white coins were firm. New Yangbu tip and new japonica rice showed a slight softening trend. New Du tip arrived in small quantities and rose several fen. Old Bu tip and old guest tip prices were firm.

Hardware: Dong White Iron will have incoming goods

Since the disaster in Osaka, where Dong White Iron was hit by a typhoon, deliveries have been cut off. As a result, the local market has seen soaring prices. The trend is so strong that it is almost unique in Shanghai. The price of 3-foot 6-inch sheets has risen to 1.26-1.27 yuan per sheet, and 3-foot 7-inch sheets are estimated at 1.45-1.46 yuan per sheet. However, customers who are slow to purchase are generally unable to buy the goods. According to news from the tea house yesterday, a foreign firm revealed that Dong goods will be available in Shanghai around the 20th of this month, as all the machines have been restored.

However, only the raw material for Western black iron sheet has fallen. Therefore, the local market may change in the future.

Free Talk

Celebrating the Double Tenth Festival 234

— Xiang Yu

I remember that the American poet Whitman, in his essay "Democratic Vistas," mentioned that the United States was already a democratic government, while Asian countries such as China and Turkey were still extremely autocratic regimes. He deeply felt that this was something for America to be proud of. Who knew that several decades later, a wave of revolution would rise in East Asia, overthrowing the autocratic regimes of thousands of years. Therefore, the Xinhai Revolution, in itself, had special significance. In other words, although the Xinhai Revolution could not contribute to the whole world like the French Revolution, the sudden thunderclap in the thick autocratic atmosphere of Asia naturally caused a lot of waves among Asian nations. This is what we can say.

However, some people may say that the United States embarked on the path of constitutionalism after the revolution, while China has been in a chaotic situation for more than twenty years since the revolution, and they feel emotional about the future of the country. In fact, this is not surprising. We must know that the United States' path to constitutionalism was not achieved overnight. At the beginning of the founding of the country, there were also party struggles, and political stability was only achieved after a civil war. It is not that Americans are descendants of the Anglo-Saxons. The Anglo-Saxon character, as the British political theorist Burke said, has always had a spirit of love for freedom. They follow their past traditions, and the success of a democratic government is naturally easier. The legacy of Chinese history is exactly the opposite. Under such circumstances, it is naturally easy to be exploited by politicians and warlords.

This year is the 23rd anniversary of the Xinhai Revolution. "After great chaos, there must be great order." If the chaos of the past many years has been great enough, then the hope for the future is not far away. This year's Double Tenth Festival is even more worthy of special commemoration.

Mourning the Neighbor to the East, Celebrating the Neighbor to the West 235

— TK

Double Tenth Night 236

— Shen Shengshi

Three young men, all wearing Western suits, two wearing peaked caps, and another tall man wearing a tilted felt hat.

With red eyes, staggering around, mumbling, they turned out of the door of a tavern.

On Double Tenth Festival, the streets of the city were filled with party flags and national flags hanging in front of shops. Banners advertising "Double Tenth Big Bargain" were everywhere. The loudspeakers and drums on the upper windows of the shops beat powerfully. The streets were more lively than usual.

— It's Double Tenth Festival!

— It's a day to look for happiness!

— Let's have a good time all night long!

They laughed, ha ha.

— Today is National Day!

— National Day is a good day for us!

The three of them danced and gesticulated on the street. The tall man held a thin cigar, and the two wearing peaked caps whistled.

— It's the song of the Double Tenth Festival!

— Who says it isn't?

Under the streetlights, the smiling girls swayed their waists, walking in front, one after another.

The three men quickened their pace, following closely behind.

— Today is a day to look for happiness!

Then, they confusedly took the women into a room on the fifth floor.

The glaring electric light, the peach-colored wallpaper, the calendar on the wall was red.

The tall man hugged the woman, kissing her, the smile on her crimson lips becoming a line. He took his felt hat, which had been with him for several years of wandering, and put it on the woman's head, completely covering her eyes and nose.

Everyone laughed.

— Today is the Double Tenth Festival!

— Give us a smile, girl.

— Girl, sing a National Day song!

— Sing it! Our whistle is a better mandolin than anything else!

The woman shook her head with a smile. She couldn't sing such a song.

The room was filled with the strong smell of wine and the mixed aroma of cigar and face powder.

Intoxicated dusk!

The lantern parade of elementary school students passed through the street below the foreign building. The street was filled with the cheers of young lives.

In the room upstairs, a few intoxicated hearts heard the slightly disturbing sounds and felt uneasy.

One of the men wearing a peaked cap jumped up, closed the window, and then drew the curtains.

After the street quieted down, a few beggars sucking in the cold wind were left, wriggling on the cement ground; in the dim streetlights, they stared blankly—

The Double Tenth Festival of the 23rd year of the Republic of China has passed again!

The Longmian Rural School as I Saw It 237

— Tian Long

Before discussing the topic, I would like to briefly talk about the culture and education of Tongcheng. In the past, Tongcheng indeed had several teachers and respected scholars who struggled to maintain it for hundreds of years, and they still enjoyed a little bit of a reputation at home and abroad. Now, it is extremely declining!

Education is related to culture. Since culture is declining, education is also lagging behind. However, Tongcheng was one of the earliest places to open schools. After the Sino-Japanese War, the whole country advocated reform. Mr. Wu Zhipu returned from Japan after studying education and was the first to open a school in his hometown. In terms of age, it is almost a twin brother of "Peking University." Today, the school founded by Mr. Wu still exists in name, but in essence, it is difficult for us to describe it!

To the north of Tongcheng, close to "Mount Longmian," connecting to Mount Tianzhu and Mount Qian, a continuous mountain range of thousands of miles, green and unbroken. Millions of people in the mountains rely on carrying firewood and selling charcoal to make a living. These poor friends and their children have no chance to know "words," and "education" is even more irrelevant to them.

More than twenty years after the founding of the Republic of China, there was a man in Tongcheng who studied elementary education, surnamed Wang, named Huaying. He wanted to independently run a "Longmian Rural School" in this mountain. First, he came to me to discuss it, and I strongly agreed. But I deplored that my life was too short, and I had to run around all year to find food. If I were to run such an education to help out-of-school people, I would be ashamed! I am a clay Bodhisattva. Although I have the heart to save the world, if I were to rescue people from the water, I am afraid that I could not protect myself. I saw that he had great motives, so I, based on my enthusiasm, planned for him: how to get started, how to arrange things, how to teach, and finally, I encouraged him a few words: "Wu Xun of Shandong was a beggar, and he was able to single-handedly found schools in Tangyi, Linqing, and Guantao counties. Liang Rengong wrote a biography for him, and the Ministry of Education praised him, making him famous at home and abroad. Moreover, you are someone who studied education?"

His belief became even more determined from then on. He abandoned all his duties and focused on the "Longmian Rural School." (Various newspapers in Anhui and Shanghai have reported on this matter.) Now, it has actually been opened for a long time.

Here, I would also like to interject and describe the purpose of his running this school, which is to adopt the principle of integrating construction and education. Although there are fixed rooms for classrooms, mobile classrooms are used in the form of open-air lectures. Textbooks are taken from the real objects of nature (agriculture, such as forests, fruits, grains, vegetables, etc.; industry, such as wood, iron, copper, tin, etc.). Students are all recruited from farmers and workers and their children, regardless of age or level. However, teaching must be divided into categories. After each subject is taught, it is called "completion of the course," not "graduation." Generally speaking, those who study in this school are all capable of producing. They produce while receiving education, which is very much in line with the conditions of "production education" and "education production."

Finally, I would like to briefly describe the landscape of this place. Mr. Dai Nanshan once used the four words "beauty surpassing human decline" to praise it. It is a pity that although the mountains and rivers are beautiful, education and culture are not commensurate! It is as if an ugly woman with a broken lip and missing teeth is wearing an extremely gorgeous and colorful dress. Passers-by cannot help but shake their heads and say, "What a waste of silk!" Famous mountains and scenic spots are mutually comparable with humanities. Tongcheng already has the natural scenery of "beauty surpassing human decline," and education and culture are so backward. Isn't it also making the mountain spirits lose their color? Now that this brand-new school has suddenly appeared, it is not only the fortune of the local area, but also adding a lot of color to the mountain spirits!

Double Tenth Memories 238

— Ai Wu

At the end of the Qing Dynasty, I was very young, so I don't know anything about the Double Tenth Revolution at that time, but the small changes that occurred at home are still vaguely remembered today.

It was a late autumn morning. Although frost had not yet appeared in the fields, the lined clothes we were wearing were not enough to keep us warm. My idle uncle took me to the earthen wall outside the door, leaned against the mulberry tree with half-yellow leaves, and sat on the stone roller (used by farmers to flatten the soil).

In the fields warmed by the sun, broad beans had just sprouted tender seedlings an inch or two long from the moist black soil, but the dragon's whisker vegetables were already growing lush green, densely covering the fields. The land prepared for planting wheat had also been turned over, facing the clear autumn sky, emitting the fresh smell of mud. This was a very good time of late autumn in the Chengdu plains.

"Ah!"

My uncle suddenly exclaimed with a gasp. I immediately followed his eyes to look. It turned out that on the small road with pink and white wild chrysanthemums beside the field with dragon's whisker vegetables, six or seven strong men in short clothes and black cloth hoods were walking towards us, all with short knives with sheaths made of raw yellow cowhide hanging on their waists. As for whether they had guns, I couldn't remember.

"Ah, Zhenzhen wa'er!" (The two characters "wa'er" must be pronounced as one sound)

My uncle recognized an acquaintance and muttered to himself in a low voice like this, but he didn't shout it out. But the crab-faced man at the head waved his hand holding the knife handle from afar, and shouted to my uncle in a loud voice:

"Old Mo! Do you recognize me? Go tell your uncle that Grandpa Chen is here!"

He knew that my father and my uncle called my grandfather "uncle." My uncle was so frightened that his face turned red and he couldn't answer for a while.

At this time, my grandfather, having been informed by someone, had already led the brown mule used for irrigating the fields out of the door. With a frightened face, his lips trembled and he said:

"Old—" He had just uttered this one word, and then quickly changed his words, "Brother Chen, the mu—mule, you, you can take it."

The crab-faced man took the mule's reins from my grandfather, and at the same time widened his eyes and swung his chin to the left.

"Do you know? Old man! The government troops are coming soon. At that time, one knife for each person, one knife for each person, big and small, none will be left!"

Saying this, he swept his fierce eyes across me. Later, when I dreamed at night, if I encountered scary bandits, they would mostly have a crab's face and such a pair of terrible eyes.

He climbed onto the back of the big mule and said happily:

"Don't be afraid! Don't be afraid! Damn the government troops!"

Before leaving, he turned his head and shouted rudely at my grandfather:

"Don't worry! Old man, I'll return it to you when I beat back the government troops!"

After they left, my grandfather told us to go inside and quickly close the gate tightly.

At this time, my grandmother hobbled out of the house with her small feet, constantly wiping her wet hands on her blue cloth apron, and scolded my grandfather in a trembling voice:

"What are we going to do to irrigate the fields next year! You, you, were still cursing last night: whoever takes your mule, you would fight with them to the death... You today... It's you yourself..."

At this time, my grandfather seemed to want to completely explode the anger he had been holding back, and he croaked back sharply:

"Everyone is rebelling now, if I don't give it to him, he will come in and rob you clean... even your clothes, even your pants!"

... ... ...

The next afternoon, my uncle carried me on his back, and my grandfather, grandmother, mother, and others, carrying luggage, left home together. My father and some other people stayed behind.

After my father sent us for a while, when he turned to leave, he told everyone:

"Sleep close to the earthen wall at night! Bullets will go through wooden boards."

Because my father had been to school, and recently visited Grandpa Pao at the market to become sworn brothers, and joined the anti-Qing Tongzhi Association, he knew that the government troops were already using foreign guns.

"Understood!"

My mother seemed to be answering with tears in her eyes.

Thinking about it now, this was the first time I had ever been a refugee. But we didn't flee far, only to a relative's house two or three miles away.

A few days later, my father came to pick us up, saying that the revolution had succeeded and there was no more fighting, and we could return home safely. But when we got home, my grandfather found that the people who had stayed at home had killed all the chickens and ducks to eat, and had also lost the mule, so he scolded angrily for a while, and turned from being unfair to being dissatisfied with the family. Every year around the Double Tenth Festival, if the family talked about this escape, my grandfather would become especially dark-faced and scold people for no reason.

Now, having been away from my hometown for nine years, I don't know how many wars it has suffered. Thinking of my grandfather, who had suffered so much from being a refugee, he should have been peaceful about the past by this year's Double Tenth Festival.

Take it down! We want to welcome the lantern parade! 239

— TK

Mr. Village Chief (2)(10)(3) 240

— Wang Renshu

Kai Yangma, who was sitting in the lower seat, felt it was necessary to mediate this argument because he was the host. He picked up the wine pot and poured a full cup for Mr. Dasheng, then poured wine for Mr. Feng Wen, Old Muren... in turn.

"Please drink! Don't keep nagging about those nonsense things. On the anniversary of the grandfather's death, shouldn't the descendants have a good drink? Uncle Muren, don't worry about those things either. The boat will naturally go straight when it reaches the bridge gate. Will our subordinates let the predecessors eat the dates! When that time comes, when Awen becomes the village chief, will he not arrange a suitable position for you?"

This remark caused the people sitting on the side to exclaim good. Ah Xian, who was sitting on the edge of the bed, and Ah De Huoyan, who was sitting on a small bamboo chair, both nodded.

"Yes! Uncle Dasheng is of course only seeing things one way, pushing away and not caring... However, I think it's not certain whether there will be a second extraction. There's no need to talk about things getting bad now." Ah Xian joined in, saying. Ah Xian lived next door to Kai Yangma's house. But now he didn't come to eat the anniversary meal. He came empty-handed to hear the news.

"Yes! I think there won't be a second ex—" Ah De Huoyan also said in a hoarse voice.

"There won't be a second extraction? Tsk, hum!" Mr. Dasheng's civilized voice came again. "There will definitely be an extraction! Definitely an extraction! The World War is coming, so surely we Chinese have to have some preparation? Everyone needs military training! Every able-bodied man needs military train! My child Wuda, he's also receiving military training at school! Humph! World War!"

A room full of surprised eyes, one by one, floated up. This pitch-black house, with gray corners everywhere, was now clearly reflected in everyone's eyes. The worn-out bed, used as a front and back partition, laden with a bed full of dust, lay gaspingly across the back. The sound of stir-frying vegetables and washing dishes also came over from the inner room.
